Book of Hajj / Exceeding the time and adding ihram. A Makkan who intends Hajj, and a mutamatti' who completed his umrah, and both left the Haram and assumed ihram. The author said: 'he did not begin a ritual'; because if he assumed ihram and began a ritual, then returned to the miqat making talbiyah, the blood is not dropped by consensus. And he said: 'and made talbiyah' to avoid their statement: 'returning to the miqat as a muhrim is sufficient' for dropping the blood according to them. But according to Abu Hanifa, he must return as a muhrim making talbiyah. (A Makkan who intends Hajj, and a mutamatti' who completed his umrah, and both left the Haram and assumed ihram: an analogy to the preceding issue concerning the obligation of blood. For the ihram of the Makkan from the Haram, and the mutamatti' by umrah, when he entered Mecca and performed umrah, he became a Makkan, and his ihram is from the Haram, so both are obligated blood for exceeding the miqat without ihram. If a Kufi enters the garden for a need, it is lost in its time, so the blood is not dropped from him. (1) His statement: 'sufficient'; because the obligation upon him is to be a muhrim at the miqat, not to initiate ihram at it. Do you not see that if he assumed ihram before reaching the miqat, then passed the miqat as a muhrim and did not make talbiyah at the miqat, nothing is obligatory upon him. And according to him, he returns making talbiyah as a muhrim, because when he reached the miqat as a non-muhrim, talbiyah and ihram became obligatory upon him at the miqat. If he left that by passing until he assumed ihram beyond the miqat, then returned, if he made talbiyah, he performed all that was due from him, so it is dropped; if he did not make talbiyah, he did not perform what was due, so the blood is not dropped from him until he makes talbiyah. As in al-Nihayah. [2] His statement: 'like a Makkan'; i.e., just as blood is obligatory on a Makkan, i.e., one who is from the people of Mecca intending Hajj, he assumed ihram for Hajj from al-Hill, and likewise the mutamatti' who assumed ihram for umrah in the months of Hajj from the miqat, entered Mecca and performed umrah, became free from his ihram and resided in Mecca, then assumed ihram for Hajj outside the Haram. [3] His statement: 'Kufi'; i.e., one from the people of Kufa, by way of example, and likewise Bostan Bani Amir is mentioned, for the ruling applies to every non-Makkan who does not intend to enter Mecca, but a place in al-Hill between the miqat and Mecca. [4] His statement: 'for a need'; to avoid the case where he intends to enter a place in al-Hill merely to pass through to page 646. [1] 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'Ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. [2] 'So he may enter Mecca without ihram, and his time is the garden like the gardener, and nothing is upon them.' So he may enter Mecca without ihram, and his time is the garden like the gardener: Bostan Bani Amir is a place inside the miqat, outside the Haram. If he enters it for a need, ihram is not obligatory upon him because it is not subject to veneration. If he enters it, he joins its people, and its people are permitted to enter Mecca without ihram. However, if he intends Hajj, his time is the garden: i.e., all al-Hill between the garden and the Haram like the gardener. (And nothing is upon them): i.e., nothing upon the gardener and upon the one who enters it. Mecca, for it is not permissible for him to enter except as a muhrim. Then this intention is only considered if it is before exceeding the miqat or at it. After exceeding, the intention of need is not considered, because the blood is due for exceeding the miqat unless he returns. As in al-Bada'i' and al-Bahr. [1] His statement: 'so he may': i.e., he is permitted to enter Mecca from the garden without ihram, and nothing is obligatory upon him, because ihram from the miqat is only obligatory on one who intends to enter Mecca. So one who intends a place in al-Hill, even if near it, ihram is not obligatory upon him at the miqat. When he enters that place, he becomes its resident, and the miqat of the one inside the miqat is that place. [2] His statement: 'a place': near Mecca inside the miqat, outside the Haram, which is now called Nakhlat Muhammad. As mentioned by Ibn Kamal. Others said: from it to Mecca is twenty-four miles. Al-Nawawi reported from some of our companions: this village is on the left facing the Kaaba when standing at Arafat. Al-Saruji mentioned: it is near Mount Arafat on the road from Iraq and Kufa to Mecca. As in Radd al-Muhtar. [3] His statement: 'because it': i.e., that place is from al-Hill. (4) His statement: 'he joins its people': whether he intends to reside there or not. [5] His statement: 'i.e., all etc.': by this he indicated that the meaning of his statement 'his time is the garden' is not that it is a time exclusively for him to the exclusion of others absolutely, but rather what is meant is al-Hill between the garden and the Haram. [6] His statement: 'and nothing is upon them': i.e., blood is not obligatory upon them if they assume ihram from al-Hill, the garden or otherwise, and go to Arafat and stand there, for they have assumed ihram from their miqat.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding the miqat and ihram by the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. It opens with two scenarios: a Makkan who intends Hajj and a mutamatti' who completed umrah; both left the Haram and assumed ihram. The commentary explains that they are analogous to a prior issue where blood (dam) is obligatory for passing the miqat without ihram. Specifically, the Makkan's ihram is from the Haram itself, and the mutamatti' becomes a Makkan after umrah, so both incur dam if they pass the miqat without ihram. The text then addresses the condition for dropping the dam when one returns to the miqat after having passed it without ihram. The author notes the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Abu Hanifa requires that the person return to the miqat as a muhrim and also make talbiyah; the Sahibayn hold that returning as a muhrim alone is sufficient. The commentary on 'kaaf' explains that the obligation is to be in the state of ihram at the miqat, not to initiate ihram there; if one passes the miqat as a non-muhrim, he must return and make talbiyah to fulfill what was due. The passage then shifts to the case of a Kufi entering Bostan Bani Amir for a need. The ruling is that such a person does not need to assume ihram to enter Bostan, and if he then intends to enter Mecca, his miqat becomes Bostan itself. The commentary clarifies that Bostan is inside the miqat but outside the Haram, so ihram is not required for entering it. The people of Bostan can enter Mecca without ihram, but their time for Hajj is the entire zone between Bostan and the Haram. If they proceed to Arafat from there, no blood is due because they have ihram from their respective miqat.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): The specific boundary (time and place) set for entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
تلبية (talbiyah): The utterance 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' upon assuming ihram, considered an integral part of ihram according to Abu Hanifa.
دم (dam): A sacrificial penalty (blood) for violating prohibitions or obligations during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is required for dropping the dam when one returns to the miqat after passing it without ihram?
A) Returning as a muhrim only
B) Returning as a muhrim and making talbiyah
C) Returning and performing two rak'ahs of prayer
D) Returning and making a vow

Key Takeaway
Passing the miqat without ihram incurs a wajib dam; to drop it when returning, Abu Hanifa requires both ihram and talbiyah.

Entering a Location Inside the Miqat for a Need: Exemption from Ihram
Commentary on exception for entering Bostan for need and its effect on miqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a person entering a place like Bostan Bani Amir for a need does not require ihram, and explain how this affects the miqat for a subsequent Hajj.

Core Idea
Entering a location inside the miqat for a need does not require ihram; but if one later intends Hajj, that location becomes his miqat.

Not every entry into a location beyond the miqat requires ihram. The classical Hanafi texts discuss the case of Bostan Bani Amir, a place inside the miqat but outside the Haram. If a person (e.g., a Kufi) enters it for a legitimate need, he may do so without ihram. However, this ruling has implications for when he later intends Hajj: his miqat shifts from the original miqat to that location. This lesson clarifies this nuanced ruling and its connection to the obligation of dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location
What is Bostan Bani Amir? Determine its geographic status: inside the miqat but outside the Haram.
The commentary describes it as a place near Mecca, inside the miqat, outside the Haram.
2
Understand the purpose
The person enters this place for a need (hajah), not intending to enter Mecca. What is the ruling on ihram in this case?
The text says: 'if he enters it for a need, ihram is not obligatory upon him because it is not subject to veneration (laysa bi wajib al-ta'zim).'
3
Apply the consequence
If that person later intends to perform Hajj, what becomes his miqat? The text states: 'his time (miqat) is the garden (all al-Hill between the garden and the Haram).'
This means he may assume ihram from that place, and no dam is due for passing the original miqat.
4
Distinguish from the earlier case
Contrast this scenario with the previous lesson: here the person never intended to enter Mecca, so no dam is incurred for passing the original miqat because he did not pass it with the intention of entering Mecca.
The commentary clarifies: 'ihram from the miqat is only obligatory for one who intends to enter Mecca.'

Book of Hajj / Exceeding the time and adding ihram. A Makkan who intends Hajj, and a mutamatti' who completed his umrah, and both left the Haram and assumed ihram. intermediate

The Miqat of al-Bustan and Entering Mecca Without Ihram for Residents
Explanation of the ruling for residents of al-Bustan and the hill regarding entering Mecca without ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for residents of al-Bustan and those within the hill regarding entering Mecca without ihram and identify the condition of intention.

Core Idea
Residents within the miqat may enter Mecca without ihram if they do not intend Hajj or Umrah.

This lesson clarifies the special status of al-Bustan, a place within the outer miqat but outside the Haram. It explains when a person may enter Mecca without assuming ihram and when it becomes obligatory. The key principle is that the miqat for those already within its boundaries is their current location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location of al-Bustan
Understand that al-Bustan is inside the miqat but outside the Haram. This determines that its residents are already within the miqat boundaries.
2
Distinguish the intention for entry
If one enters for a need unrelated to Hajj or Umrah, ihram is not required. If intending Hajj, the miqat extends to the entire hill between al-Bustan and the Haram.
The hill (al-hill) is the open land outside the Haram.
3
Apply the rule for those within the hill
Any person residing in or passing through the hill may enter Mecca without ihram because their miqat is that place.
This includes residents of al-Bustan and others inside the miqat.
4
Recognize the exception after crossing the miqat
If one crosses the miqat without ihram even for a need, a dam is required unless they return to the miqat before entering Mecca.
The intention of need is only considered before or at the miqat crossing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فله دخول مكة غير محرم ووقته البستان كالبستاني ولا شيء عليهما) : بستان بني عامر موضع داخل الميقات، خارج الحرم، فإذا دخله لحاجة لا يجب عليه الإحرام؛ لكونه غير واجب التعظيم، فإذا دخله التحق بأهله، ويجوز لأهلِهِ دخول مكة غير محرم؛ لكن إن أراد الحج، فَوَقْتُهُ البستان: أي جميع الحل الذي بين البستان والحرمِ كالبستاني. (ولا شيء عليهما): أي لا شيء على البستاني، وعلى مَن دخل مكة، فإنّه لا يحل له الدخول إلا محرماً، ثمّ هذا القصد إنما يعتبر إذا كان قبل مجاوزة الميقات أو عندها، وأما بعد المجاوزة فلا يعتبر قصد الحاجة؛ لكون الدم بالمجاوزة عن الميقات ما لم يرجع. كذا في «البدائع» و«البحر». (1) قوله: فله؛ أي يجوز له أن يدخل مكة من البستان بدون الإحرام، ولا يلزم عليه شيء؛ لأنّ الإحرام من الميقات إنّما يلزم لمن أراد دخول مكة، فمن أراد مكاناً من الحل ولو كان قريباً منها لم يجب عليه الإحرام عند الميقات، فإذا دخل ذلك الموضع صار بأهله، ومن هو داخل الميقات ميقاته ذلك الموضع. (2) قوله: موضع؛ قريب مكة داخل الميقات خارج الحرم، وهي التي تسمى الآن نخلة محمد، كذا ذكره ابن كمال، وقال غيره: إنَّ منه إلى مكة أربعة وعشرون ميلاً، وقال النووي نقلاً عن بعض أصحابنا: هذه القرية على يسار مستقبل الكعبة إذا وقف بأرض عرفات، وذكر السروجي: إنَّه بالقرب من جبل عرفات على طريق العراق والكوفة إلى مكة. كذا في رد المحتار). (3) قوله: لكونه؛ أي ذلك الموضع من الحلّ. (4) قوله: التحق بأهله؛ سواء نوى فيه الإقامة أو لا. (5) قوله: أي جميع... الخ؛ أشار بهذا إلى أنه ليس المراد بقوله: «وقته البستان»: كونه وقتاً له بعينه دون غيره مطلقاً، بل المراد به الحلّ الذي بين البستان وبين الحرم. (6) قوله: ولا شيء عليهما؛ أي لا يجب عليه دم إذا أحرما من الحلّ: البستان أو غيره، فذهبا بعرفة، ووقفا به، فإنّهما أحرما من ميقاتهما. (1) «البحر الرائق (3: 48)» (2) (رد المحتار (2) : 581).

ثم يقال: إن أحرما من الحل ووقفا بعرفة؛ لأنهما أحرما من ميقاتهما. (ومن دخل مكة بلا إحرام لزمه حج أو عمرة، وصح منه لو حج عما عليه في عامه ذلك، لا بعده. جاوز وقته فأحرم بعمرة وأفسدها، مضى وقضى، ولا دم عليه؛ لترك الوقت)، فإنه يصير قاضياً حق الميقات بالإحرام منه في القضاء. [1] قوله: لزمه حج أو عمرة؛ فإنّه كان الواجب عليه أن يدخل الحرم بإحرام لأحدهما تعظيماً لتلك البقعة، فإذا تركه ذلك لزمه أحدهما. [2] قوله: وصح منه... الخ؛ يعني إذا دخل الحرم بغير إحرامه فلزمه بذلك حج أو عمرة فخرج إلى الميقات وأحرم بأحدهما، الواجب عليه بسبب آخر كحجة الإسلام وحجة النذر والعمرة المنذورة، فإنّه يجزئه ذلك عمّا لزمه بالدخول بغير إحرام وإن لم ينوه، وهذا إذا كان ذلك في ذلك العام؛ لأنه تلافي المتروك في وقته، فإن أتى به في سنة أخرى لا يجزئه؛ لأنّ الأول صار ديناً في ذمته فلا يتأدى إلا بإحرام مقصود. [3] قوله: وأفسدها؛ أي تلك العمرة بإتيان ما يفسده. [4] قوله: مضى؛ أي يجب عليه أن يتم تلك العمرة ويقضيها بعده. [0] قوله: فإنه يصير... الخ؛ يعني يتأدى حق الميقات بإحرامه لقضاء العمرة منه، ولو أحرم في القضاء من ميقاتِ المكيّ لا يسقط الدم عنه. كذا في «البحر»(1). (1) «البحر الرائق» (3 : 52).
So he may enter Mecca without being in ihram, and his time (miqat) is al-Bustan like the resident of al-Bustan, and nothing is required of them. (So he may enter Mecca without being in ihram, and his time (miqat) is al-Bustan like the resident of al-Bustan): Bustan Bani Amir is a place within the miqat, outside the Haram. If he enters it for a need, ihram is not obligatory upon him because it is not necessarily venerated. So if he enters it, he joins his family, and it is permissible for his family to enter Mecca without ihram. But if he intends Hajj, his time (miqat) is al-Bustan: that is, all the open country (al-hill) between al-Bustan and the Haram, like the resident of al-Bustan. (And nothing is required of them): i.e., nothing is required of the resident of al-Bustan and the one who entered Mecca; then this intention is only considered if it is before or at the crossing of the miqat. As for after crossing, the intention of need is not considered because the blood (dam) is due due to crossing the miqat unless he returns. Thus in al-Bada'i' and al-Bahr. (1) His saying: So he may; i.e., it is permissible for him to enter Mecca from al-Bustan without ihram, and nothing is binding on him because ihram from the miqat is only binding on one who intends to enter Mecca. So if one intends a place in the hill (al-hill) even if it is near to it, ihram is not obligatory at the miqat. Then if he enters that place, he becomes like its inhabitant, and whoever is within the miqat, his miqat is that place. (2) His saying: place; near Mecca, within the miqat, outside the Haram, and it is now called Nakhlat Muhammad, as Ibn Kamal mentioned. Others said: from it to Mecca is 24 miles. Al-Nawawi narrated from some of our companions: this village is on the left of the direction of the Ka'ba when one stands at the land of 'Arafat. Al-Saruji mentioned: it is near the mountain of 'Arafat on the road of Iraq and Kufa to Mecca. Thus in Radd al-Muhtar). (3) His saying: because it is; i.e., that place is part of the hill (al-hill). (4) His saying: joins his family; whether he intended to stay there or not. (5) His saying: That is, all... etc.; he indicated by this that the meaning of his saying 'his time is al-Bustan' is not that it is a specific time for him alone absolutely, but rather it means the hill (al-hill) between al-Bustan and the Haram. (6) His saying: And nothing is required of them; i.e., no blood sacrifice (dam) is required of them if they assume ihram from the hill: al-Bustan or elsewhere, and they go to 'Arafat and stand there, because they have assumed ihram from their miqat. (1) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (3:48) (2) Radd al-Muhtar (2:581).

Then it is said: If they assume ihram from the hill and stand at 'Arafat, because they assumed ihram from their miqat. (And whoever enters Mecca without ihram, Hajj or 'Umrah becomes obligatory upon him, and it is valid from him if he performs Hajj for what is due upon him in that same year, not after. If he crossed his time and assumed ihram for 'Umrah and spoils it, he continues and makes it up, and there is no blood sacrifice (dam) upon him due to leaving the time (miqat)), because he becomes one who fulfills the right of the miqat by assuming ihram from it in the makeup. [1] His saying: Hajj or 'Umrah becomes obligatory upon him; because it was obligatory upon him to enter the Haram with ihram for one of them as veneration for that place, so when he omitted that, one of them becomes obligatory upon him. [2] His saying: And it is valid from him... etc.; meaning if he entered the Haram without ihram and consequently Hajj or 'Umrah became obligatory for him, and then he went out to the miqat and assumed ihram for one of them, which is obligatory for another reason like the Hajj of Islam (the obligatory Hajj) or a vowed Hajj or a vowed 'Umrah, then that suffices for what became obligatory due to entering without ihram even if he did not intend it, and this is if that is in the same year because he made up for the omitted act in its time. But if he performs it in another year, it does not suffice because the first became a debt in his liability and is only discharged by a specific ihram. [3] His saying: And spoils it; i.e., that 'Umrah by doing something that invalidates it. [4] His saying: He continues; i.e., he must complete that 'Umrah and make it up afterwards. [0] His saying: Because he becomes... etc.; meaning the right of the miqat is fulfilled by his ihram for the makeup of the 'Umrah from it, and if he assumes ihram in the makeup from the miqat of the Meccan (i.e., from the Haram), the blood sacrifice (dam) is not waived from him. Thus in al-Bahr (1). (1) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (3:52).
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings related to the miqat and entering Mecca without ihram. It begins by clarifying the status of the place called al-Bustan (Bustan Bani Amir), a location within the miqat but outside the Haram. The ruling states that residents of al-Bustan may enter Mecca without ihram because their miqat is that area; if they intend Hajj, however, their miqat is the entire hill between al-Bustan and the Haram. The passage then emphasizes that the intention of need only matters if one has not yet crossed the miqat; after crossing, a dam is required unless one returns. The commentary elaborates on the definition of al-Bustan, noting its distance from Mecca and that it is now called Nakhlat Muhammad. It also clarifies that when a person from the hill (al-hill) enters a place within the miqat, that place becomes his miqat. Next, the passage addresses the case of someone who enters Mecca without ihram: he must perform either Hajj or 'Umrah due to his violation. If he then performs Hajj for his own obligation (e.g., the obligatory Hajj of Islam) in the same year, it suffices for both obligations, but not if done in a later year. If he enters into 'Umrah and spoils it, he must continue and make it up, and he owes no dam for missing the miqat because his ihram for the makeup fulfills the obligation of the miqat. The commentary clarifies that if one makes up the 'Umrah from the miqat of the Meccan (within the Haram), the dam is not waived. All these rulings are supported by references to Al-Bada'i' and Al-Bahr, indicating their reliability in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
البستان (al-Bustan): A place (Bustan Bani Amir) located within the miqat but outside the Haram, near Mecca. It is considered part of the hill (al-hill) and serves as the miqat for its residents.
الميقات (al-miqat): The boundary point from which one must assume ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah. For residents within the miqat, their miqat is their place of residence.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, marked by specific clothing and prohibitions. It must be entered at the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the miqat for a resident of al-Bustan who intends to perform Hajj?
A) Al-Bustan itself
B) The entire hill between al-Bustan and the Haram
C) The Haram boundary
D) The place where he assumes ihram

Key Takeaway
The miqat of the resident is his residence; he may enter Mecca without ihram unless he intends Hajj or Umrah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Consequences of Entering Mecca Without Ihram
Explanation of the obligation upon entering Mecca without ihram and how it is fulfilled.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the obligation incurred by entering Mecca without ihram and state when it is fulfilled by performing Hajj or Umrah in the same year.

Core Idea
Entering Mecca without ihram makes Hajj or Umrah obligatory, but it is fulfilled if performed in the same year for one's own obligation.

This lesson addresses the penalty for crossing the miqat without assuming ihram. It explains that one who enters Mecca without ihram must perform either Hajj or Umrah as a veneration for the Haram. The ruling also details that if he performs his obligatory Hajj in the same year, it suffices for both obligations. Additionally, it covers the case of spoiling a compensatory Umrah and the waiver of the dam for missing the miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act that triggers the obligation
Entering Mecca without ihram (and without intending Hajj/Umrah) makes it wajib to perform either Hajj or Umrah. This is because the Haram must be entered with reverence.
2
Determine the fulfillment condition
If the person performs Hajj (or Umrah) for his own duty (e.g., Hajj al-Islam) in the same year, it suffices for the obligation incurred, even without specific intention.
The key is that it is done in the same year. If performed in a later year, it does not suffice.
3
Analyze the case of spoiling the Umrah
If one enters ihram for Umrah (as the penalty) and spoils it, he must complete and make up the Umrah. No dam is due for missing the miqat because the makeup ihram from the miqat fulfills that right.
The makeup ihram must be from the miqat, not from within the Haram, otherwise the dam remains.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
A person from outside the miqat who enters Mecca for business without ihram must perform Hajj or Umrah within the same year. If he later performs the obligatory Hajj, that suffices.
He must go out to the miqat to assume ihram for that Hajj/Umrah.

This passage presents several rulings related to the miqat and entering Mecca without ihram. Next, the passage addresses the case of someone who enters Mecca without ihram: he must perform either Hajj or 'Umrah due to his violation. If he then performs Hajj for his own obligation (e.g., the obligatory Hajj of Islam) in the same year, it suffices for both obligations, but not if done in a later year. If he enters into 'Umrah and spoils it, he must continue and make it up, and he owes no dam for missing the miqat because his ihram for the makeup fulfills the obligation of the miqat. The commentary clarifies that if one makes up the 'Umrah from the miqat of the Meccan (within the Haram), the dam is not waived. All these rulings are supported by references to Al-Bada'i' and Al-Bahr, indicating their reliability in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
البستان (al-Bustan): A place (Bustan Bani Amir) located within the miqat but outside the Haram, near Mecca. It is considered part of the hill (al-hill) and serves as the miqat for its residents.
الميقات (al-miqat): The boundary point from which one must assume ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah. For residents within the miqat, their miqat is their place of residence.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, marked by specific clothing and prohibitions. It must be entered at the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person enters Mecca without ihram and later in the same year performs a vowed Umrah, does it suffice for the penalty?
A) Yes, because any obligatory Hajj/Umrah in the same year suffices.
B) No, only the Hajj of Islam suffices.
C) Yes, but only if specifically intended for the penalty.
D) No, he must perform a separate Umrah explicitly for the penalty.

Key Takeaway
Entering Mecca without ihram makes Hajj or Umrah obligatory; it is fulfilled if performed in the same year for one's own obligation.

Ruling on Entering Makkah Without Ihram
Commentary on entering Makkah without ihram and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation incurred by entering Makkah without ihram and explain when a substitute Hajj or Umrah suffices.

Core Idea
Entering Makkah without ihram makes Hajj or Umrah wajib; performing another obligatory Hajj in the same year fulfills it.

Veneration of the Haram requires entering with ihram. The commentary explains that omitting this obligation creates a compensatory duty of Hajj or Umrah. However, if you perform an already obligatory Hajj (like Hajj al-Islam) in the same year, it suffices without separate intention. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
Recognize that entering the Haram with ihram for Hajj or Umrah is wajib as a form of veneration (تعظيماً لتلك البقعة). This is the basis for the penalty of omission.
2
Understand the compensatory obligation
If one enters without ihram, a Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory (لزمه حج أو عمرة). This is because the original wajib was omitted, so a substitute is required.
The substitute is not a penalty but a fulfillment of the right of the miqat.
3
Determine when the substitute suffices
If the person performs another obligatory Hajj (e.g., Hajj al-Islam) in the same year, it suffices for the substitute obligation, even without specific intention. This is because the omission is made up within its time.
If performed in a later year, it does not suffice; a specific intention is then required.
4
Analyze the case of spoiling a delayed Umrah
If one passes the miqat without ihram (exceeds the time) and then performs Umrah and spoils it, they must complete it and make it up. No blood sacrifice is due because the qada ihram from the miqat fulfills the miqat's right.
If qada ihram is done from the Makkan miqat (within Haram), dam is required.

Chapter of Hajj: Exceeding the time and adding the ihram. If two (people) perform ihram from the Hill and stand at Arafat, and whoever enters Makkah without ihram, a Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory upon him. And it is valid from him if he performs Hajj for what is upon him in that same year, not after it. (And whoever enters Makkah without ihram, a Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory upon him, and it is valid from him if he performs Hajj for what is upon him in that same year, not after it. [1] His saying: 'a Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory upon him' — because it was obligatory upon him to enter the Haram with ihram for one of them as veneration for that place. [2] His saying: 'and it is valid from him...' etc. — meaning: if he entered the Haram without ihram, then a Hajj or Umrah became obligatory upon him due to that, then he goes out to the miqat and performs ihram for one of them that is obligatory upon him for another reason, like the Hajj of Islam or a vowed Hajj or vowed Umrah, then that suffices for what became obligatory upon him by entering without ihram, even if he did not intend it. And this is if that is in that same year; because he made up for the omitted (act) in its time. But if he performs it in another year, it does not suffice; because the first (obligation) became a debt in his liability, so it is not fulfilled except by a purposeful ihram. [3] His saying: 'and spoils it' — meaning that Umrah by doing what spoils it. [4] His saying: 'he continues' — meaning he must complete that Umrah and make it up afterward. [0] His saying: 'then he becomes...' etc. — meaning that the right of the miqat is fulfilled by his ihram for the make-up of the Umrah from it. And if he performs ihram in the make-up from the miqat of the Makkan (i.e., the miqat for residents of Makkah), the blood sacrifice is not remitted from him. Thus in 'al-Bahr' (3:52).
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from the chapter of Hajj dealing with rulings related to entering Makkah without ihram and the consequences. The matn states several interconnected rulings:
1. If two persons (likely a man and his wife, or two men) perform ihram from the Hill (al-hill, the area outside the Haram) and then stand at Arafat, their Hajj is valid because they performed ihram from their miqat (the appointed place). The comment explains this simply.
2. Whoever enters Makkah without ihram is obligated to perform either a Hajj or an Umrah. The commentator explains that originally it was obligatory to enter the Haram with ihram for one of these acts out of veneration for the sacred place. Since he omitted that, one of them becomes obligatory upon him. This is a compensatory obligation.
3. If after incurring this obligation, he then goes to the miqat and performs ihram for a different obligatory Hajj or Umrah (such as the Hajj al-Islam or a vowed pilgrimage) in the same year, that performance suffices for the obligation incurred by entering without ihram, even if he did not intend it as a substitute. This is because he made up for the omitted duty (entering with ihram) within its proper time (the same year). However, if he performs it in a later year, it does not suffice because the original obligation became a fixed debt on his liability and requires a specific intention.
4. If a person passes the miqat without ihram (i.e., 'exceeds his time') and then later performs ihram for Umrah and spoils it, he must continue that Umrah (complete it despite the spoilage) and then make it up afterwards. No blood sacrifice (dam) is required for leaving the miqat time because his ihram for the make-up (qada) fulfills the right of the miqat. The commentator clarifies that he becomes a 'qadi' (one who performs qada), and the right of the miqat is considered fulfilled by his ihram from the miqat for the make-up. However, if he were to perform ihram for the make-up from the miqat of the Makkans (i.e., from within the Haram, as residents do), the blood sacrifice would not be waived.
The commentary provides the reasoning for each ruling, rooted in the concept of miqat obligations and the timing of fulfillment. The authority is from the Hanafi school, quoting al-Bahr al-Raiq as a source.

Key Terms
الحل (al-hill): The area outside the Haram of Makkah, where non-residents should assume ihram.
الميقات (al-miqat): The appointed place for entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by intention and talbiyah.
القضاء (al-qada): The performance of a missed or spoiled Hajj or Umrah after its original time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only if performed in the same year
B) In any year after the incident
C) Only if performed with the specific intention of fulfilling that obligation
D) It never suffices

Key Takeaway
Entering Makkah without ihram obligates a substitute Hajj or Umrah; performing another obligatory Hajj in the same year fulfills it automatically.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Abandoning Hajj or Umrah for a Makki
Intra-Hanafi dispute on abandoning one ihram when adding hajj to 'umrah for a Makki.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Makki who adds hajj to an ongoing 'umrah and evaluate the arguments of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A Makki who starts 'umrah must abandon a later hajj, because the commenced 'umrah is stronger.

When a resident of Mecca begins 'umrah by performing tawaf and then intends to add hajj, a legal problem arises: one of the two ihrams must be abandoned. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on which ihram to abandon and why. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to apply the principle that once an act of worship is commenced, it gains legal strength.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note the key factors: the person is a Makki (resident of Mecca), has begun 'umrah with at least one circuit of tawaf, and then forms the intention for hajj.
The same ruling would apply if more circuits were performed, but not if the 'umrah was already completed.
2
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa rules that the hajj ihram must be abandoned (rafḍ) with a dam (blood penalty), and the 'umrah is completed. A separate hajj is performed later.
The dam is wajib for abandoning an ihram.
3
State the ruling of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that the 'umrah must be abandoned, and the person proceeds with hajj, making up the 'umrah later.
Their reasoning focuses on the lesser significance and ease of making up 'umrah.
4
Analyze the legal reasoning (dalil)
Abu Hanifa argues that the 'umrah ihram is strengthened by having begun its actions (shurū‘ fī af‘ālihā), so it is more established. The Sahibayn argue that combining both for a Makki is not legislated, so the one that is easier to make up ('umrah) should be abandoned.
The dispute is over which ihram has greater legal weight after commencement.
5
Distinguish the Afaqi case
An Afaqi (non-resident) in the same situation proceeds with hajj, because building hajj actions upon 'umrah actions is valid for him. No abandonment is needed.
This contrast clarifies that the Makki’s restriction is based on his status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام
مكي طاف لعمرته شوطاً، فأحرم بالحج رفضه وعليه دم، وحج وعمرة.
[قوله مكي قيده به لأن الآفاقي إن أحرم بعمرة فطاف لها شوطاً، ثم أحرم بحجة يمضي في الحج؛ لأن بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة في حقه صحيح. كذا في «البناية»]
[قوله رفضه بفعل شيء من محظورات الإحرام بعد التحلل من العمرة]
[قوله لأجل الرفض بالفتح: مصدر رفض يرفض من باب طلب وضرب]
[قوله لأنه فائتُ الحج بنقض إحرامه، وحكمه: أن يتحلل بعمرة ثم يأتي بالحج من قابل]
[قوله يرفض العمرة وذلك لأنه لا بد من ترك أحدهما؛ لأن الجمع بينهما في حق المكي غير مشروع، والعمرة أولى بالرفض؛ لأنها أدنى حالاً وأقل أعمالاً، وأيسر قضاء، لكونها غير مؤقتة، والحج مؤقت بذي الحجة. وله: أن إحرام العمرة تأكد بالشروع في أفعالها، فكان رفض إحرام الحج الذي لم يشرع في مناسكه أولى]

Chapter on adding Ihram to Ihram. A Makki performed one circuit of Tawaf for his Umrah, then intended Hajj—he abandons it and owes a blood penalty, and (performs) Hajj and Umrah. Thus in 'al-Binayah'.] [His saying 'he abandons it': by doing something from the prohibitions of Ihram after becoming free from Umrah.] [His saying 'because of abandonment' (rafḍ): with fathah, it is the masdar of rafaḍa yarfiḍu from the patterns of ṭalaba and ḍaraba.] [His saying 'because he is one who misses the Hajj': by breaking his Ihram; its ruling: that he should be released with an Umrah then come with Hajj next year.] [His saying 'he abandons the Umrah': that is because it is necessary to leave one of them; because combining them in the case of a Makki is not legislated, and the Umrah is more deserving of abandonment because it is lesser in condition and fewer in actions, and easier to make up, since it is not time-bound, while Hajj is time-bound to Dhul-Hijjah. And for him: that the Ihram of Umrah is strengthened by beginning its actions, so abandoning the Ihram of Hajj, which he has not begun its rites, is more appropriate.] [His saying 'four circuits': he indicates by it that the mention of 'one circuit' in the matn is incidental, and the ruling...]
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with the chapter on adding one ihram to another. It presents a ruling followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The case: a Makki (resident of Mecca) performs one circuit (shaut) of tawaf for his 'umrah, then intends hajj by entering ihram for it. According to Abu Hanifa, he must abandon (yarfudu) the hajj ihram, pay a dam (blood penalty) for the abandonment, and then perform both hajj and 'umrah separately (the 'umrah is completed, and hajj is made up later). The reasoning: the 'umrah ihram has been strengthened by beginning its actions (tawaf), so it is more established; thus, the later hajj ihram, which has not yet begun its rites, is abandoned. However, according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is the 'umrah that should be abandoned, not the hajj. Their reasoning: for a Makki, combining 'umrah and hajj in one journey is not legislated, so one must be abandoned; since 'umrah is less significant, not time-bound, and easier to make up, it is more appropriate to abandon it. The passage also clarifies that the ruling differs for an Afaqi (one from outside Mecca): if an Afaqi begins 'umrah then intends hajj, he may proceed with hajj because his hajj actions can be built upon his 'umrah actions. The mention of 'one circuit' in the matn is incidental; the same ruling applies even if he had performed more than one circuit, but if he had completed four circuits (i.e., most of the tawaf), then according to some, the ruling may differ (the text cuts off). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the structure of the text.

Key Terms
رفض (rafḍ): To abandon or annul an ihram; in this context, the legal act of relinquishing a second ihram after already being in a valid ihram.
مكي (Makki): A resident of Mecca (within the Haram boundaries); for him, combining 'umrah and hajj in one journey is not allowed.
آفاقي (Afaqi): A person from outside the miqat; for him, building hajj actions upon 'umrah actions is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what should a Makki do if he performs one circuit of tawaf for 'umrah and then intends hajj?
A) Abandon the hajj and pay a dam, then perform both hajj and 'umrah.
B) Abandon the 'umrah and proceed with hajj, making up 'umrah later.
C) Continue with both ihrams and combine them without penalty.
D) Cancel both and start anew.

Key Takeaway
When a Makki has commenced 'umrah and intends hajj, the mufta bihi view is to abandon the hajj with a dam, because the 'umrah is strengthened by beginning its actions.

Ruling for a Makkan Adding Hajj to 'Umrah
Ruling for a Makkan adding Hajj to 'Umrah after starting tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Makkan adds Hajj to an ongoing 'Umrah, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding which ihram to reject.

Core Idea
A Makkan who starts 'Umrah and then intends Hajj must reject one; Abu Hanifa rejects the Hajj, Sahibayn reject the 'Umrah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj where a Makkan has already begun his 'Umrah (performed some tawaf) and then decides to add the ihram of Hajj. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling distinguishing between the situation of a Makkan and a non-Makkan (afaqi). An important intra-madhhab difference arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding which ihram should be rejected. Understanding this dispute reveals the underlying legal principles of strengthening of actions and practical convenience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
A Makkan who performed one circuit of tawaf for 'Umrah and then enters ihram for Hajj. The ruling: he rejects the Hajj ihram, owes a dam, and performs both separately.
The text explicitly states this is for a Makkan; a non-Makkan proceeds with Hajj instead.
2
Understand the reasoning for rejecting the Hajj
Abu Hanifa's view is that the 'Umrah ihram has been strengthened by the commencement of its actions (tawaf), so it is more appropriate to reject the later Hajj ihram.
The principle: an ihram that has begun its actions is stronger than one that has not.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's opposing view
They argue that since Hajj is time-specific (Dhul-Hijjah) and 'Umrah can be done anytime, it is more practical to reject the 'Umrah and preserve the Hajj.
Practical convenience (al-taysir) is a factor in their reasoning.
4
Note the agreement when tawaf reaches four circuits
If the Makkan has performed four or more circuits, all imams agree that the Hajj is rejected because the 'Umrah is too far advanced.
Four circuits mark the point where the 'Umrah becomes firmly established.
5
Determine the consequence if he completes both despite prohibition
Both acts are valid (legal prohibition confirms legality) but he becomes sinful and must sacrifice a compensatory animal (dam jabar).
The principle: al-nahy 'an al-af'al al-shar'iyyah yuthbit al-mashru'iyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قصر أو لا. ثم الشرح: قوله مكي: قيده به لأن الآفاقي إن أحرم بعمرة فطاف لها شوطاً، ثم أحرم بحجة يمضي في الحج؛ لأن بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة في حقه صحيح. كذا في البناية. قوله رفضه: بفعل شيء من شوطاً؛ لأنه لو طاف أربعة أشواط يرفض إحرام الحج اتفاقاً. يختلف في الشوط والشوطين والثلاثة، وبالجملة ما دام طاف أقل من أربعة يرفض العمرة عندهما، وإحرام الحج عنده، وأما إذا طاف أكثر أشواط طواف العمرة يصير آثماً. قوله وذبح: أي يجب عليه أن يذبح هدياً وهو دم جبر في حق المكي. قوله والنهي الخ: دفع دخل مقدر، تقرير الدخل: أن القرآن لما كان منهياً للمكي فكيف يصح منه لو فعله، فإن بين الصحة والنهي منافاة، وتقرير الدفع: أن النهي عن الأفعال الشرعية يثبت كونها مشروعة، فإن النهي لا يصح عند وجود القدرة الشرعية، فيلزم منه أنه لو فعله يترتب عليه آثره، وإن صار آثماً، وقد حقق ذلك في كتب الأصول. قوله للنقصان: أي في أداء النسك؛ لكون المكي ممنوعاً عن القرآن. قوله ومن أحرم بالحج: يوم النحر؛ قيد به لأنه لو أحرم بآخر بعرفات ليلاً أو نهاراً رفض الثانية، وعليه دم الرفض وحجة وعمرة. قوله لزمه الآخر: فيبقى محرماً إلى السنة الثانية إلى أن يؤديه. قوله قصر أو لا: أي إذا لم يحلق ولم يقصر للأول، ثم أحرم بالثاني، لزمه دم، سواء حلق عقيب الإحرام الثاني أو لم يحلق، بل أخره حتى حج وحلق في العام القابل؛ لجنايته على إحرامه الثاني بالتقصير، أو إحرامه الأول بالتأخير، وهذا عنده. وعندهما: لا دم فيما إذا لم يحلق؛ لأنهما لا يوجبان بالتأخير شيئاً. قال في النهاية: إنما عبر بالتقصير؛ لأن وضع المسألة يتناول الذكور والإناث، فذكر أولاً لفظ الحلق ثم ذكر التقصير؛ لأن الأفضل في حق الرجال الحلق، وفي حق النساء القصر.
Chapter on adding ihram to ihram. A Makkan who performed one tawaf for his 'Umrah and then entered ihram for Hajj rejects it and owes a blood sacrifice, and performs Hajj and 'Umrah. If he completes both, it is valid and he sacrifices. And whoever entered ihram for Hajj, performed Hajj, and then on the day of Nahr (sacrifice) enters ihram for another (Hajj), if he shaves for the first, the second becomes incumbent on him without blood; otherwise, with a blood sacrifice whether he shortens (hair) or not. Then the commentary: His saying 'Makkan': he restricted it because if a non-Makkan enters ihram for 'Umrah, performs one tawaf for it, then enters ihram for Hajj, he proceeds with the Hajj; because building the actions of Hajj upon the actions of 'Umrah is valid in his case. As in al-Binaya. His saying 'rejects it': by doing something from the prohibitions of ihram after the tahlil of 'Umrah. His saying 'because of rejection': with fatha: verbal noun of rafada from the pattern of talaba and daraba. And Hajj and 'Umrah; because his Hajj is lost, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): he rejects the 'Umrah unanimously. And he only said: he performed one tawaf; because if he performed four tawafs, he rejects the ihram of Hajj unanimously. There is difference regarding one, two, or three tawafs; in summary, as long as he performed less than four, he rejects the 'Umrah according to them, and the ihram of Hajj according to him. And if he performed more than the tawafs of 'Umrah, he rejects the Hajj unanimously among our imams. His saying: 'If he completes both, it is valid and he sacrifices': because he performed the actions of both, but he is prohibited from doing so, and prohibition of legal actions confirms legality; however, a blood sacrifice is required due to deficiency. His saying 'valid': i.e., each of them; because he has fulfilled what he committed to, but he becomes sinful. His saying 'and sacrifices': i.e., he must slaughter a sacrificial animal which is a compensatory blood sacrifice for the Makkan. His saying 'and the prohibition...': repelling a potential objection; the objection is: since performing both (qiran) is prohibited for the Makkan, how can it be valid from him? For validity and prohibition conflict. The repelling: the prohibition of legal actions confirms their legality; for prohibition is not valid without legal capacity, so if he does it, its effects follow, even though he becomes sinful. This has been verified in usul works. His saying 'due to deficiency': i.e., in performing the pilgrimage; because the Makkan is prohibited from qiran. His saying 'and whoever enters ihram for Hajj': on the day of Nahr; he restricted it because if he enters ihram for another at 'Arafat by night or day, he rejects the second, and owes a blood sacrifice for rejection and performs Hajj and 'Umrah. His saying 'the second becomes incumbent on him': he remains in ihram until the second year until he performs it. His saying 'whether he shortens or not': i.e., if he did not shave or shorten for the first, then entered ihram for the second, a blood sacrifice becomes incumbent on him, whether he shaves immediately after the second ihram or does not shave, but delays it until he performs Hajj and shaves the following year; due to his violation of his second ihram by shortening or of his first by delay. This is according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to them (Sahibayn): no blood if he did not shave; because they do not obligate anything due to delay. It is said in al-Nihaya: he only used the term 'shortening' because the issue covers both men and women; so he first mentioned shaving and then shortening, because for men shaving is preferable, and for women shortening.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah explains two distinct rulings concerning adding one ihram to another. The first ruling involves a Makkan who has begun the tawaf of his 'Umrah (one circuit) and then intends to add the ihram of Hajj. The ruling explicitly states that he should reject the Hajj ihram and owes a blood sacrifice (dam), and then he performs both Hajj and 'Umrah separately. The commentary clarifies that this applies specifically to a Makkan, because a non-Makkan (afaqi) who does the same would instead proceed with the Hajj, since for him it is valid to build the actions of Hajj upon those of 'Umrah. It also explains the meaning of 'rejection' as doing something that violates the prohibitions of ihram after having already partially completed the 'Umrah. A key internal Hanafi difference is highlighted: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the later Hajj ihram is rejected, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the earlier 'Umrah ihram is rejected. The commentary explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the 'Umrah ihram has been strengthened by commencing its actions (tawaf), so it is more appropriate to reject the Hajj ihram which has not yet started its rites. The Sahibayn argue that since combining both pilgrimages is not permitted for a Makkan, the 'Umrah is easier to make up as it is not time-specific, while Hajj is fixed to Dhul-Hijjah. However, if the Makkan had performed four or more circuits of tawaf, then all three imams agree that he rejects the Hajj ihram, because the 'Umrah has become too advanced. If despite the prohibition he completes both, the ruling is that both are valid due to the principle that a prohibition on a legal action presupposes the possibility of its existence, but he becomes sinful and must sacrifice a compensatory animal (dam jabar) for the deficiency in performing the pilgrimage (since qiran is prohibited for a Makkan). The second ruling concerns a person who has already completed his Hajj and then, on the day of Nahr (the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah), enters ihram for another Hajj. If he shaves for the first Hajj before entering the second, then the second Hajj becomes incumbent upon him and he must perform it the following year, without any additional blood sacrifice due to asl al-ahdath? Actually, the text says 'bila dam' (without blood) when he shaves for the first. If he does not shave (or shorten his hair) for the first Hajj, then he owes a blood sacrifice whether he subsequently shaves or not, because he has violated his second ihram by delaying the tahlil of the first. Here again there is a difference: Abu Hanifa obligates the dam in that case, while the Sahibayn do not obligate anything due to delay alone. The commentary also notes that the text mentions 'qasr' (shortening) alongside 'halq' (shaving) to include women, for whom shortening is the sunnah.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Rejection of an ihram by intentionally violating its prohibitions (e.g., wearing sewn clothes, applying perfume) to exit the state of ihram.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required as compensation for violating the rules of ihram or for deficiency in the pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a Makkan performs one tawaf of 'Umrah and then enters ihram for Hajj, what must he do?
A) Reject the 'Umrah and proceed with Hajj
B) Reject the Hajj and continue with 'Umrah
C) Perform both and sacrifice two animals
D) Cancel both pilgrimages and start anew

Key Takeaway
A Makkan who starts 'Umrah and then intends Hajj must reject one; Abu Hanifa rejects Hajj, Sahibayn reject 'Umrah; if completed despite prohibition, both are valid but sin and dam are incurred.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Second Hajj on the Day of Nahr
Ruling for adding a second Hajj on the day of Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when someone who has completed Hajj enters ihram for a second Hajj on the day of Nahr, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the blood sacrifice.

Core Idea
If you shave for your first Hajj before a second on Nahr, the second becomes incumbent without dam; otherwise, a dam is wajib (Abu Hanifa) but not according to Sahibayn.

This lesson covers a unique scenario: a person has already performed Hajj and then, on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah), enters ihram for another Hajj. The ruling depends on whether he has performed tahlil (shaving or shortening hair) for the first Hajj. An intra-Hanafi difference arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the obligation of a blood sacrifice when tahlil is delayed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
After completing Hajj, on the day of Nahr, the person enters ihram for a second Hajj.
The text restricts this to the day of Nahr; if done at 'Arafat, the ruling differs.
2
Note the first condition: if he shaved for the first Hajj
If he shaved (halq) or shortened (qasr) his hair for the first Hajj before entering the second ihram, then the second Hajj becomes incumbent (lazim) on him without any blood sacrifice.
He must perform the second Hajj the following year.
3
If he did not shave for the first Hajj
If he did not shave or shorten for the first Hajj, then he owes a blood sacrifice (dam) regardless of whether he shaves later. This is according to Abu Hanifa.
The dam is wajib due to jinaayah (violation) on the second ihram or delay of the first.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn do not obligate a dam in this case because they do not consider delay in tahlil as a violation requiring compensation.
They only obligate dam if the person shaves after the second ihram, but not for delay alone.
5
Understand the reasoning
Abu Hanifa considers that the person has violated his second ihram by delaying the tahlil of the first (or by shortening after the second), hence a dam is wajib for jinaayah.
The commentary mentions 'jinaayatahu 'ala ihramihi al-thani bil-taqsir aw ihramihi al-awwal bil-ta'khir'.

Source Text

قصر أو لا. ثم الشرح: قوله مكي: قيده به لأن الآفاقي إن أحرم بعمرة فطاف لها شوطاً، ثم أحرم بحجة يمضي في الحج؛ لأن بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة في حقه صحيح. كذا في البناية. قوله رفضه: بفعل شيء من Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, one of the actions of tahlil (exiting ihram).
قصر (qasr): Shortening the hair (by cutting a portion), the alternative for women in tahlil; also acceptable for men but less preferred than shaving.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a person completes Hajj and then enters ihram for another Hajj on the day of Nahr without shaving for the first, what must he do?
A) He must perform the second Hajj and sacrifice a dam.
B) He must reject the second ihram and perform 'Umrah instead.

Key Takeaway
If you add a second Hajj on the day of Nahr, shaving for the first before the second spares you a dam; if you haven't shaved, Abu Hanifa obligates a dam, but Sahibayn do not.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Validity of Qiran for a Makkan and Required Dam
Ruling on completing both Hajj and Umrah in Qiran for a Makkan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Makkan performing Qiran and apply the usul principle that prohibition of a Shar'i act confirms its legislated nature.

Core Idea
Prohibition does not invalidate; the Makkan's Qiran is valid but requires dam.

This passage from `Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a key Hanafi ruling: if a Makkan performs Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) despite the prohibition, his acts are valid but deficient, requiring a compensatory sacrifice (dam jabr). The commentary clarifies the legal principle behind this: the prohibition (nahy) of a Shar'i act does not negate its validity; rather, it confirms the act as legislated (mashru') while imposing a penalty for the deficiency. Let's unpack this ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is a Makkan performing Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but requires a dam (slaughter). Also, the person becomes sinful (athim).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the usul principle: 'al-nahy 'an al-af'al al-shar'iyyah yuhaqqiqu al-mashru'iyyah' — the prohibition of a Shar'i act establishes it as legislated. This means the act has legal effects even if performed despite prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the principle prove validity? The commentary explains that if the act were completely invalid, the prohibition would have no meaning. Since prohibition implies the capacity to perform (qudrah shar'iyyah), performing it brings its effects, though with sin. Thus validity is derived from the nature of the prohibition itself.
4
Note the dam's basis
The dam is wajib because of the deficiency (nuqsan) in performing the ritual. The Makkan is prohibited from Qiran, so his performance is deficient, requiring compensation to perfect the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو أتمهما صح وذبح ) ؛ لأنه أتى بأفعالهما ، لكنه منهي عنه ، والنهي عن الأفعالِ الشَّرعيّةِ يحقق المشروعيَّة ؛ لكن يجب دم للنقصان.
[1] قوله : صح ؛ أي كل منهما ؛ لأنه أتى بما التزمه، لكنه يصير اثماً. [٢]قوله : وذبح ؛ أي يجب عليه أن يذبح هدياً وهو دم جبر في حق المكي. [٣] قوله : والنهي ... الخ ; دفعُ دخل مقدر ، تقرير الدخل : أن القرآنَ لَمَّا كان منهياً للمكي فكيف يصح منه لو فعله، فإن بين الصحة والنهي منافاة، وتقرير الدفع : أن النهي عن الأفعال الشرعيّة يثبتُ كونها مشروعة، فإنّ النهي لا يصح عند وجود القدرة الشرعية، فيلزم منه أنه لو فعله يترتب عليه آثره ، وإن صار آثماً، وقد حقق ذلك في كتب الأصول. [٤]قوله : للنقصان ; أي في أداء النُّسُك ; لكون المكي ممنوعاً عن القرآن.
If he completes both, it is valid and he must slaughter. Because he performed their acts, but he is prohibited from this. The prohibition of Shar'i acts confirms their legislated nature, but a dam (sacrifice) is obligatory due to deficiency. [1] He said: 'Valid' means each of them; because he fulfilled what he committed to, but he becomes sinful. [2] He said: 'slaughter' means he must slaughter a hady, which is a compensatory dam for a Makkan. [3] He said: 'The prohibition... etc.' is a rebuttal of a presumed objection. The explanation of the objection: Since Qiran is prohibited for a Makkan, how can it be valid if he does it? Because there is a contradiction between validity and prohibition. The rebuttal: The prohibition of Shar'i acts establishes them as legislated, because prohibition is not valid when there is Shar'i capacity. It follows that if he does it, its effects apply, even though he becomes sinful. This is established in works of Usul. [4] He said: 'due to deficiency' means in performing the ritual, because the Makkan is prevented from Qiran.
Source pages p. 650

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case of a Makkan who performs Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) despite being prohibited from doing so. The matn states that if he completes both, the acts are valid and he must slaughter a hady. The commentary explains that validity here means both acts are legally effective, though he commits a sin by doing something prohibited. A potential objection arises: how can an act be both prohibited and valid? The response is a foundational usul principle: prohibition (nahy) in acts of worship indicates their legislated nature (mashru'iyya) and does not automatically invalidate them. The prohibition here is not about the essence of the acts but about the deficiency in their perfection (qadr al-kamal), so the acts are valid but deficient, requiring compensation (dam). The dam is obligatory due to the deficiency in performing the ritual (nuqsan), because a Makkan is forbidden from Qiran (as per preferred view). This is a clear application of Hanafi usul: nahy that does not reach the core of the act leaves it valid but may entail compensation.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory sacrifice (hady) required to make up for a deficiency in performing a ritual.
المكي (al-Makki): A resident of Makkah, for whom Qiran is prohibited (according to the matn).
النهي عن الأفعال الشرعية يحقق المشروعية (al-nahy 'an al-af'al al-shar'iyyah yuhaqqiqu al-mashru'iyyah): The principle that prohibition of a Shar'i act does not negate its legislated nature; it confirms its status as an act of worship with legal effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a Makkan who performs Qiran still have valid Hajj and Umrah despite the prohibition?
A) Because the prohibition is only advisory (makruh tanzihi).
B) Because the prohibition of a Shar'i act confirms its legislated nature and does not invalidate the act.
C) Because the Makkan was ignorant of the prohibition.
D) Because the dam automatically removes the sin.

Key Takeaway
A prohibited act of worship can still be valid; the key distinction is between invalidity and deficiency, with the latter requiring compensation (dam).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Dam for Delaying Halq/Taqsir in Hajj
Ruling on entering second Hajj on Day of Nahr and necessity of dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of dam when a pilgrim delays halq/taqsir before entering a second Hajj on the Day of Nahr, and state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Delaying halq/taqsir incurs a dam according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

This passage presents a subtle intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The scenario involves a pilgrim who performs Hajj and then, on the Day of Nahr before shaving or shortening his hair, enters a second ihram for the following year's Hajj. The question is whether delaying the halq/taqsir triggers a compensation (dam). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how different usul principles (e.g., whether delay constitutes a jinayah) shape fiqh rulings even within a single school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person enters ihram for Hajj, performs Hajj, and then on the Day of Nahr enters a second ihram for Hajj (for the next year). The key variable is whether he has performed halq or taqsir for the first Hajj before this second ihram.
The passage specifies 'Day of Nahr' (10th Dhul Hijjah), not Arafat; a separate rule applies if the second ihram is at Arafat.
2
State the ruling when halq/taqsir is done
If he shaved or shortened for the first Hajj before entering the second ihram, the second Hajj becomes binding but without any additional dam. This is agreed upon.
3
State the ruling when halq/taqsir is delayed
If he did not shave or shorten for the first, and then enters the second ihram, a dam is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn hold that no dam is required.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that the delay constitutes a jinayah (harm) on the ihrams: either it harms the second ihram by delaying its completion (taqsir), or it harms the first ihram by prolonging the state of ihram (ta'khir). This harm requires compensation via a dam.
The phrase 'qad jana 'ala ihramihi al-thani bi al-taqsir aw ihramihi al-awwal bi al-ta'khir' encapsulates his rationale.
5
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning and the practical consequence
The Sahibayn do not consider mere delay as a cause for dam; delay alone does not violate the integrity of the ihram. Thus, in practice, followers of Abu Hanifa will require a dam while followers of the Sahibayn will not. Later Hanafi practice generally follows Abu Hanifa's view.
The passage does not explicitly resolve the tarjih, but the majority of later Hanafi scholars adopted Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أحرم بالحج، وحجّ، ثم يوم النحر بآخر، فإن حَلَقَ للأَوَّلِ لَزِمَهُ الآخر، بلا دم، وإلا فمع دم قصر أو لا)
يختلفُ في الشوط والشوطين والثلاثة، وبالجملة ما دام طاف أقل من أربعة يرفض العمرة عندهما ، وإحرام الحج عنده ، وأما إذا طاف أكثر أشواط طوافِ العمرة يرفضُ الحج اتفاقاً بين أئمتنا.
(٥) قوله : يوم النحر ; قيد به لأنه لو أحرم بآخر بعرفات ليلاً أو نهاراً رفض الثانية، وعليه دم الرفض وحجة وعمرة.
[٦] قوله : لزمه الآخر ; فيبقى محرماً إلى السنة الثانية إلى أن يؤديه. (۷) قوله : قصر أو لا ; أي إذا لم يحلق ولم يقصر للأول، ثم أحرم بالثاني، لَزِمَه دم، سواء حلق عقيب الإحرام الثاني أو لم يحلق ، بل أخَّرَه حتى حج وحلق في العام القابل ; لجنايته على إحرامه الثاني بالتقصير ، أو إحرامه الأول بالتأخير، وهذا عنده. وعندهما : لا دم فيما إذا لم يحلق ; لأنهما لا يوجبان بالتأخير شيئاً، قال في «النهاية»: إنما عبر بالتقصير ; لأنّ وضع المسألة يتناول الذكور والاناث، فذكر أولاً لفظ الحلق ثم ذكر التقصير ; لأنّ الأفضل في حق الرجال الحلق، وفي حق النساء القصر.
(أي إن أحرم بالحج وحجّ، ثُمَّ أحرم يوم النحر بحجة أخرى في العام القابل، فإن حلق للأَوَّل قبل هذا الإحرام لَزِمَهُ الآخرُ بلا دَم ، وإن لم يَحْلِقُ لَزِمَهُ الآخرُ مع دم.)
Whoever entered ihram for Hajj, performed Hajj, then on the Day of Nahr entered [another] [Hajj], if he shaved [halq] for the first, the second becomes binding on him without a dam; otherwise, with a dam, whether he did taqsir (shortening) or not. The difference is in one, two, or three circuits; in short, as long as he has performed less than four circuits, he can revoke the Umrah according to them [Sahibayn], and the Hajj ihram according to him [Abu Hanifa]; but if he performed more circuits of the Umrah tawaf, he revokes the Hajj by consensus of our Imams.
[5] He said: 'on the Day of Nahr' – it is restricted because if he had entered a second [ihram] at Arafat, night or day, he revokes the second, and on him is a dam of revocation and [he performs] a Hajj and an Umrah. [6] He said: 'the second becomes binding on him' – he remains in ihram until the next year to perform it. (7) He said: 'whether he did taqsir or not' – meaning if he did not shave or shorten for the first, then entered the second, a dam is obligatory, whether he shaved immediately after the second ihram or did not shave, but delayed until he performed Hajj and shaved in the following year; because he has harmed his second ihram by delaying, or his first ihram by delaying. This according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to them (Sahibayn): there is no dam if he did not shave, because they do not impose anything for delay. He said in al-Nihaya: He expressed it by 'taqsir' because the scenario encompasses males and females; so he first mentioned halq then taqsir, because halq is better for men and taqsir for women.
(Meaning: If he entered ihram for Hajj, performed Hajj, then on the Day of Nahr entered another Hajj in the following year: if he shaved for the first before this ihram, the second is binding without dam; if he did not shave, the second is binding with dam.)
Source pages p. 650

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) concerning a person who performs Hajj and then on the Day of Nahr enters another ihram for Hajj (for the next year). The key issue is whether a dam is required when he does not perform halq or taqsir for the first Hajj before entering the second. According to Abu Hanifa, deferring the halq/taqsir until after the second ihram constitutes a harm (jinayah) to the second ihram (by delaying its completion) or to the first (by prolonging the state of ihram), thus requiring a dam. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no dam is required simply for delaying halq/taqsir, as the act of delaying does not itself violate the ihram. The commentary also clarifies that the term 'taqsir' is used alongside 'halq' to include women, as women perform taqsir instead of halq. Additionally, a subtle difference is noted: if the second ihram is entered at Arafat (before the Day of Nahr), the ruling changes—the second is revoked, requiring a dam of revocation and a full Hajj and Umrah. The passage also touches on a scenario where a person revokes an Umrah after fewer than four circuits of tawaf (according to Sahibayn) or a Hajj after more than four (consensus).

Key Terms
الرفض (al-rafḍ): Revocation or annulment of an ihram due to entering a conflicting second ihram.
دم الرفض (dam al-rafḍ): A compulsory dam for revoking an ihram (e.g., when revoking a second ihram entered at Arafat).
الحلق والتقصير (al-ḥalq wa al-taqṣīr): Shaving the head (halq) or shortening the hair (taqsir) to exit ihram; halq is for men, taqsir for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a dam obligatory when a person does not shave (halq) for the first Hajj before entering a second Hajj on the Day of Nahr?
A) Because he missed the sunnah of shaving.
B) Because the delay in shaving harms the second ihram or prolongs the first.
C) Because he is now combining two Hajjs in one year, which is prohibited.
D) Because the second Hajj is invalid without a dam.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of dam for delaying halq/taqsir before a second Hajj depends on whether delay is considered a jinayah; a core disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Combining Two Umrahs: Obligation of Dam
Ruling on combining two Umrahs before completing the first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on combining two Umrahs and identify when a dam becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Combining two Umrahs without completing the first is makruh tahrimi and requires a dam.

This lesson focuses on a specific scenario: a pilgrim who performs all actions of Umrah except shaving (halq) and then enters a second Umrah. The source passage explains why this is forbidden and what compensation is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is: performing all actions of Umrah except halq/taqsir, then entering a second Umrah.
Halq/taqsir is the final step of Umrah that completes it.
2
Determine the ruling
The ruling is that such an action necessitates a dam (slaughter of an animal). The reason is that the second Umrah is entered before its proper time (after halq of the first), combining two Umrah ihrams incorrectly.
3
Analyze the legal cause
Combining two Umrah ihrams is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and any violation of the rules requiring dam incurs that obligation.
Makhruh tahrimi is close to haram and requires a dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أتى بعمرة إلا الحلق، فأحرم بأخرى ذبح) ; لأنه جمع بين إحرامي العمرة، وهو مكروه فلزمه الدم. آفاقي أحرم به، ثمّ بها لزماه) ; لأنَّ الجمع بينهما مشروع في الآفاقي كالقرآن.
(وتبطل هي بالوقوف قبل أفعالها لا بالتوجه) : إي بالتوجه إلى عرفات، (فإن طاف له، ثُمَّ أحرم بها فمضى عليهما ذَبَح ) ; لأنه أتى بأفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج ، (ونُدب رفضها، فإن رفض قضى وأراق.
11 ] قوله : وإن لم يحلق ; أي للتحلل من الإحرام الأول.
[٢] قوله : ومن أتى بعمرة ... الخ ; يعني أتى جميع أفعال العمرة إلا الحلق أو التقصير، ثمّ أدخل الإحرام الثاني وجب عليه دم.
[٣] قوله : لأنه جمع ... الخ ; فإنّ وقت إحرام العمرة الثانية بعد الحلق والتقصير للأولى، فإحرامها قبل ذلك يكون إحراماً ما قبل الوقت، فيصير جامعاً بين إحرامي العمرة.
(٤) قوله : أحرم به ; أي أحرم بالحج أولاً، ثم أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يشرع في طواف القدوم.
[0]قوله : مشروع ; إلا أنه يصير مسيئاً في هذه الصورة ; لأنّ السنة في القرآن أن يحرم بهما جميعاً أو يُقدِّم إحرام العمرة على إحرام الحج. [٦]قوله : بالوقوف ; أي إذا وقف بعرفات قبل أفعال العمرة بطلت العمرة، لا بنفس التوجه إلى عرفات. [۷] قوله : وندب ; أي استحب ترك العمرة لتأكد الحج بطوافه. [۸]قوله : وأراق ; ماض من الإراقة، وهو إسالة الدم ونحوه ; أي ذبح لارتكاب
Whoever performed Umrah except for halq, then entered another Umrah: he must slaughter (dhabh). Because he combined two ihrams of Umrah, which is makruh, so dam becomes obligatory. A non-Makkan (afaqi) who entered ihram for Hajj first, then for Umrah: both are binding on him. Because combining them is legislated for a non-Makkan, like Qiran. And the Umrah is invalidated by standing at Arafat before its actions, not by merely proceeding (tawajjuh) [to Arafat]. Then if he performed tawaf for Hajj, then entered ihram for Umrah, and proceeded with both, he slaughters. Because he performed actions of Umrah upon actions of Hajj. And it is recommended (nudiba) to revoke it (the Umrah); if he revokes it, he must make it up (qada) and cause blood to flow (araqa, i.e., slaughter). [11] He said: 'and if he did not shave' means for exiting the first ihram. [2] He said: 'Whoever performed Umrah...' he means he performed all actions of Umrah except shaving or shortening (halq/taqsir), then entered the second ihram: dam is obligatory. [3] He said: 'Because he combined...' the time for entering the second Umrah is after halq/taqsir for the first; entering it before that is entering before the time, so he becomes a combiner of two Umrah ihrams. (4) He said: 'entered ihram for it' means he first entered ihram for Hajj, then entered ihram for Umrah before starting tawaf al-qudum. [5] He said: 'legislated' but he becomes a wrongdoer in this scenario because the sunnah in Qiran is to enter ihram for both together or to give precedence to Umrah over Hajj. [6] He said: 'by standing' meaning if he stands at Arafat before the actions of Umrah, the Umrah is invalidated, not by merely proceeding to Arafat. [7] He said: 'and it is recommended' meaning it is preferred to leave the Umrah because of the strength of Hajj due to its tawaf. [8] He said: 'and cause to flow' is from 'iraqah, meaning spilling blood etc.; i.e., he slaughters due to committing [the violation].
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage states several rulings related to combining Umrahs and Umrah with Hajj. First, if a person performs all acts of Umrah except halq/taqsir, then enters a second Umrah, a dam is obligatory because he combined two Umrah ihrams improperly (the proper time for the second is after completing the first). For a non-Makkan (afaqi) who enters Hajj first then Umrah before tawaf al-qudum, both become binding (i.e., Qiran is valid but the sequence is not ideal; he is considered 'musi' (wrongdoer)). If he stands at Arafat before performing the actions of Umrah (tawaf and sa'y), the Umrah is invalidated. However, merely proceeding to Arafat does not invalidate it. If he performed tawaf for Hajj (tawaf al-qudum) and then entered ihram for Umrah, and then proceeds with both, he must slaughter a dam because he performed Umrah actions after Hajj actions (the correct order is Umrah first). It is recommended (mustahabb) to revoke the Umrah in such a case; if he revokes it, he must make it up (perform a separate Umrah) and slaughter a dam for the violation. The commentary further clarifies that 'halq' in the scenario is for exiting the first ihram; the prohibition of combining two Umrahs is because the second ihram is entered before its proper time. For the afaqi, the combination (Hajj then Umrah) is legislated but not ideal; the sunnah is to enter both together or Umrah first. The invalidation of Umrah by standing at Arafat is specifically because standing (wuquf) is a main pillar of Hajj, and performing it before completing Umrah spoils the tamattu' or 'umrah-only intention.

Key Terms
دم (dam): An obligatory sacrifice in Hajj/Umrah for certain violations.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, a concluding act of Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must a dam be slaughtered when combining two Umrahs without completing the first?
A) Because two Umrahs are not allowed in one trip.
B) Because the second Umrah is entered before its permissible time, making the combination makruh.
C) Because the first Umrah was invalid.
D) Because the pilgrim didn't shave after both Umrahs.

Key Takeaway
A dam is obligatory when a second Umrah is entered before completing the first (i.e., before halq/taqsir).

Afaqi Combining Hajj and Umrah: Sequence and Ruling
Ruling on afaqi combining Hajj then Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling for a non-Makkan who enters Hajj first then Umrah, and identify the sunnah sequence.

Core Idea
For a non-Makkan, combining Hajj and Umrah is valid in any order, but the sunnah is to combine both together or Umrah first.

This lesson examines the case of an afaqi (pilgrim from outside Miqat) who first enters ihram for Hajj, then later for Umrah before performing tawaf al-qudum. The passage confirms both are binding, but notes this sequence is not ideal.

Guided Path
1
Define 'afaqi'
Afaqi means a person from outside the Miqat boundaries, for whom the Qiran type of Hajj (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is legislated.
Residents of Makkah are not afaqi and have different rules.
2
Identify the scenario
The scenario: an afaqi enters ihram for Hajj first, then later (before tawaf al-qudum) enters ihram for Umrah. This results in both being binding.
The key is that he intended Hajj first.
3
Note the ruling
Both ihrams are valid and binding, but the sequence is contrary to the sunnah. The preferred (sunnah) order is to enter ihram for both together or Umrah first.
He will be considered 'musi' (wrongdoer) for reversing the order.
4
Determine consequence
No dam is required for the sequence itself; he simply performs Qiran but with a disliked order.
Dam may be required if he does something else, but not for this.

A non-Makkan (afaqi) who entered ihram for Hajj first, then for Umrah: both are binding on him. Because combining them is legislated for a non-Makkan, like Qiran.
