(4) He said: 'entered ihram for it' means he first entered ihram for Hajj, then entered ihram for Umrah before starting tawaf al-qudum. [5] He said: 'legislated' but he becomes a wrongdoer in this scenario because the sunnah in Qiran is to enter ihram for both together or to give precedence to Umrah over Hajj. [6] He said: 'by standing' meaning if he stands at Arafat before the actions of Umrah, the Umrah is invalidated, not by merely proceeding to Arafat. [7] He said: 'and it is recommended' meaning it is preferred to leave the Umrah because of the strength of Hajj due to its tawaf. [8] He said: 'and cause to flow' is from 'iraqah, meaning spilling blood etc.; i.e., he slaughters due to committing [the violation].
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage states several rulings related to combining Umrahs and Umrah with Hajj. First, if a person performs all acts of Umrah except halq/taqsir, then enters a second Umrah, a dam is obligatory because he combined two Umrah ihrams improperly (the proper time for the second is after completing the first). For a non-Makkan (afaqi) who enters Hajj first then Umrah before tawaf al-qudum, both become binding (i.e., Qiran is valid but the sequence is not ideal; he is considered 'musi' (wrongdoer)). If he stands at Arafat before performing the actions of Umrah (tawaf and sa'y), the Umrah is invalidated. However, merely proceeding to Arafat does not invalidate it. If he performed tawaf for Hajj (tawaf al-qudum) and then entered ihram for Umrah, and then proceeds with both, he must slaughter a dam because he performed Umrah actions after Hajj actions (the correct order is Umrah first). It is recommended (mustahabb) to revoke the Umrah in such a case; if he revokes it, he must make it up (perform a separate Umrah) and slaughter a dam for the violation. The commentary further clarifies that 'halq' in the scenario is for exiting the first ihram; the prohibition of combining two Umrahs is because the second ihram is entered before its proper time. For the afaqi, the combination (Hajj then Umrah) is legislated but not ideal; the sunnah is to enter both together or Umrah first. The invalidation of Umrah by standing at Arafat is specifically because standing (wuquf) is a main pillar of Hajj, and performing it before completing Umrah spoils the tamattu' or 'umrah-only intention.

Key Terms
آفاقي (āfāqī): A pilgrim from outside the Miqat boundaries.
مسيئ (musi’): One who does something wrong but not sinful; acting contrary to sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence for an afaqi who enters Hajj first then Umrah before tawaf al-qudum?
A) The Umrah is invalid and he must restart.
B) He becomes a wrongdoer (musi’) because he reversed the sunnah order.
C) He must slaughter a dam.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
An afaqi may combine Hajj and Umrah in any order, but the sunnah is to combine together or Umrah first.

Invalidation of Umrah by Wuquf and the Recommendation to Revoke
Rulings on invalidation of Umrah by standing at Arafat and recommendation to revoke

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when Umrah is invalidated during Hajj and state the ruling on revoking it.

Core Idea
Standing at Arafat before performing Umrah actions invalidates the Umrah; merely proceeding to Arafat does not.

This lesson covers two more rulings from the source: the invalidation of Umrah if a pilgrim stands at Arafat before completing its actions, and the recommendation (undub) to revoke the Umrah in such a situation, with a requirement to make it up and slaughter a dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act that invalidates Umrah
Standing (wuquf) at Arafat before performing the actions of Umrah (tawaf and sa’y) invalidates the Umrah.
Wuquf is a pillar of Hajj; doing it before Umrah corrupts the sequence.
2
Distinguish between proceeding and standing
Merely proceeding (tawajjuh) towards Arafat does not invalidate Umrah; only actual standing does.
This is an important nuance to avoid unnecessary worry.
3
Understand the scenario of performing tawaf first
If he performs tawaf for Hajj (tawaf al-qudum), then enters ihram for Umrah, then proceeds to Arafat and stands, he must slaughter a dam because he did Umrah actions after Hajj actions.
The dam is for the incorrect order, not for the invalidation.
4
Learn the recommendation to revoke
It is recommended (nudiba) to revoke the Umrah (i.e., exit ihram for Umrah and continue only Hajj). If he revokes, he must later make up the Umrah (qada) and slaughter a dam.
Revocation is a form of 'rafd' or iftiradh.

Starting a Second Umrah Before Completing the First
Explains ruling and reason for required sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a dam is wajib when a person begins a second Umrah before halq from the first, and explain the reason based on combining two Umrah ihrams.

Core Idea
Performing a second Umrah before shaving from the first requires a sacrifice because it combines two ihrams prematurely.

Imagine you have nearly completed an Umrah—only the final shaving remains—but you start another Umrah. What is the ruling? This lesson examines a specific scenario where a person performs all actions of Umrah except halq (shaving/trimming) and then begins a second Umrah. The Hanafi school holds that this act is makruh and necessitates a dam (sacrificial animal). We will explore the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the missing element
The person has performed all actions of Umrah except shaving or trimming (halq/taqsir). This is the incomplete state of the first Umrah.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that a dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib (obligatory).
The source text uses the word 'ذبح' (slaughter) to indicate the sacrifice.
3
Understand the reason
The reason is that starting a second Umrah before completing the first creates a combination of two Umrah ihrams (jam' bayn ihramayn), which is makruh (disliked). In Hanafi fiqh, certain makruh acts require compensation (jabar).
The text states: 'لأنه جمع بين إحرامي العمرة، وهو مكروه فلزمه الدم'.
4
Note the time condition
The proper time for entering ihram for a second Umrah is after completing the first by shaving or trimming. Entering ihram before that is premature and constitutes the disliked combination.
The commentary emphasizes: 'وقت إحرام العمرة الثانية بعد الحلق والتقصير للأولى'.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may not require a dam for this act, hence the ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). However, the Hanafi position is clear.
The hanafi_position_box indicates cross_madhhab_status: 'mukhtalaf_fih'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أتى بعمرة إلا الحلق، فأحرم بأخرى ذبح (ومن أتى بعمرة إلا الحلق، فأحرم بأُخْرَى ذبح) ؛ لأنه جمع بين إحرامي العمرة، وهو مكروه فلزمه الدم. [٢] قوله : ومن أتى بعمرة ... الخ ؛ يعني أتى جميع أفعال العمرة إلا الحلق أو التقصير، ثمّ أدخل الإحرام الثاني وجب عليه دم. [٣] قوله : لأنه جمع ... الخ ؛ فإنّ وقت إحرام العمرة الثانية بعد الحلق والتقصير للأولى، فإحرامها قبل ذلك يكون إحراماً ما قبل الوقت، فيصير جامعاً بين إحرامي العمرة.
Whoever performs an Umrah except the shaving, and then begins another Umrah, must sacrifice. (Whoever performs an Umrah except the shaving, and then begins another Umrah, must sacrifice) because he has combined two ihrams of Umrah, and that is disliked, so blood becomes obligatory. [2] His statement: 'Whoever performs an Umrah...' etc. means he performed all actions of Umrah except shaving or trimming, then introduced the second ihram; blood is obligatory. [3] His statement: 'Because he combined' etc. Indeed, the time for the second Umrah's ihram is after shaving and trimming for the first, so his ihram before that is an ihram before its time, thus becoming a combiner of two ihrams of Umrah.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case of a person who performs all actions of Umrah except for shaving or trimming (halq or taqsir) and then begins a second Umrah. The ruling is that a sacrifice (dam) is wajib. The reason provided is that this act combines two ihrams of Umrah, which is makruh (disliked). The commentary clarifies that the second Umrah's proper time is after completing the first by shaving or trimming; entering ihram before that is premature and constitutes combining two Umrah ihrams. The burden is on the performer to offer a sacrifice as a compensation for the disliked act.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (e.g., sheep) required as compensation for certain violations in Hajj or Umrah.
إحرام (ihram): The sacred state of a pilgrim during Hajj or Umrah, marked by intention and specific dress.
جمع بين إحرامين (jam' bayn ihramayn): Entering into two ihrams of the same type (e.g., both for Umrah) before completing one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The second Umrah is invalid.
B) He must sacrifice a dam.
C) He must complete the first Umrah before doing the second.
D) Nothing is required.

Key Takeaway
Performing a second Umrah before halq from the first is valid but makruh, and a dam is wajib.

Afaqi Combining Hajj and Umrah: Sequence and Ruling
Ruling on an Afaqi combining Hajj and Umrah in reverse sequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an Afaqi who enters ihram for Hajj first and then for Umrah, and identify the sunnah sequence.

Core Idea
Valid but disliked: combining Hajj then Umrah binds both, but the sunnah prefers Umrah first or both together.

This passage addresses a specific case: an Afaqi (a pilgrim from outside the miqat) first enters ihram for Hajj, then before performing Tawaf al-Qudum, enters ihram for Umrah. The text rules that both ihrams are valid and binding, but notes that the person is considered a wrongdoer (musi') because the optimal sequence according to the Sunnah for Qiran is to enter both ihrams together or to begin with Umrah. Thus, while legally valid, the act is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person and Actions
The subject is an Afaqi (one who lives outside the miqat). He first enters ihram for Hajj, then, before starting Tawaf al-Qudum, enters ihram for Umrah.
Afaqi status is key because the ruling differs for residents of the miqat.
2
Determine the Ruling on Validity
Both ihrams are binding (lazimah). The combination is valid because combining Hajj and Umrah is legislated for the Afaqi, similar to Qiran.
The proof is the general permissibility of Qiran.
3
Identify the Preferred (Sunnah) Sequence
Although valid, the sequence (Hajj first, then Umrah) is not the sunnah. The sunnah for Qiran is to enter both ihrams together or to start with Umrah.
Going against the sunnah makes the act makruh tanzihi, not invalid.
4
Conclude the Legal Classification
The ruling is: sahih (valid) but makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked). The person is considered a wrongdoer (musi') due to abandoning the better practice.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آفاقي أحرم به، ثمّ بها لزماه (آفاقي أحرم به ، ثمّ بها لزماه) ؛ لأنَّ الجمع بينهما مشروع في الآفاقي كالقرآن. [٤] قوله : أحرم به ؛ أي أحرم بالحج أولاً، ثم أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يشرع في طواف القدوم. [٠] قوله : مشروع ؛ إلا أنه يصير مسيئاً في هذه الصورة ؛ لأنّ السنة في القرآن أن يحرم بهما جميعاً أو يُقدِّم إحرام العمرة على إحرام الحج.
An Afaqi who enters ihram for it (Hajj) and then for it ('Umrah) — both are binding upon him. (An Afaqi who enters ihram for it, then for it, both are binding upon him) because combining them is legislated for the Afaqi like al-Qiran. [4] His statement: 'He enters ihram for it' means he entered ihram for Hajj first, then entered ihram for Umrah before he began the Tawaf al-Qudum. [0] His statement: 'Is legislated' except that he becomes a wrongdoer in this situation because the Sunnah in al-Qiran is to enter ihram for both together or to present the ihram of Umrah over the ihram of Hajj.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding an Afaqi (a person from outside the miqat) who first enters ihram for Hajj and then enters ihram for Umrah before starting Tawaf al-Qudum. The text states that both ihrams are valid and binding. The reason is that combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey is generally permissible for the Afaqi, similar to Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram). However, the commentary notes that the person is considered sinful (musi') because the sunnah in Qiran is to either enter both ihrams together or to begin with Umrah first. Thus, although the act is legally valid, it is not in accordance with the best practice.

Key Terms
آفاقي (afaqi): A person who resides outside the miqat boundaries for Hajj.
قرآن (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single journey with one ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only the first ihram is valid.

Key Takeaway
An Afaqi who enters ihram for Hajj first then Umrah before Tawaf al-Qudum has valid ihrams but commits a disliked act by abandoning the sunnah sequence.

Invalidation of Umrah by Standing at Arafah
Specifies what invalidates Umrah when combined with Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which Umrah is invalidated when combined with Hajj, and distinguish between standing and merely heading toward Arafah.

Core Idea
Merely heading to Arafah does not invalidate Umrah; only actual standing there before completing Umrah actions does.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in Qiran Hajj (combined Hajj and Umrah). It clarifies that only the actual wuquf (standing) at Arafah, not the intention or travel toward it, nullifies the Umrah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for pilgrims performing Qiran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
Determine what worship is being discussed. The passage refers to 'Umrah' (العمرة).
2
Identify the invalidating factor
Locate the specific action that causes invalidation: standing (الوقوف) at Arafah before completing the actions of Umrah.
The text says 'بالوقوف قبل أفعالها' – by standing before its actions.
3
Identify the non-invalidating factor
Find what does NOT invalidate: heading (التوجه) toward Arafah. The commentary explains that 'heading' means merely traveling toward Arafah.
The phrase 'لا بالتوجه' – not by heading.
4
Understand the rationale (implicit)
Standing at Arafah is a major pillar of Hajj. If performed before completing Umrah, it overrides the Umrah, rendering it void. Heading is just intention and travel, which lacks such overriding effect.
This distinction is based on the strength of the ritual act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل هي بالوقوف قبل أفعالها لا بالتوجه (وتبطل هي بالوقوف قبل أفعالها لا بالتوجه) : إي بالتوجه إلى عرفات
And it ('Umrah) is invalidated by standing (at 'Arafat) before its actions, not by heading (toward 'Arafat). (And it is invalidated by standing before its actions, not by heading) i.e., by heading toward 'Arafat.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying when an Umrah becomes invalid. If a person in the state of Umrah combines it with Hajj (or is doing Qiran) and stands at 'Arafah before completing the actions of Umrah (like tawaf and sa'i), the Umrah is nullified. However, merely setting out or heading toward 'Arafah does not invalidate it. The commentary clarifies that 'tawajjuh' means heading toward 'Arafat, which is harmless.

Key Terms
الوقوف بعرفات (al-wuquf bi-Arafat): The essential stand at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah for Hajj.
الوقوف قبل أفعالها (al-wuquf qabla af'aliha): Standing at Arafah before completing the actions of Umrah (tawaf and sa'i).
التوجه (al-tawajjuh): Heading or setting out toward a place; here, heading toward Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Turning toward Arafah.
B) Standing at Arafah before Umrah actions.

D) Entering the miqat.

Key Takeaway
Standing at Arafah before completing Umrah actions invalidates the Umrah; heading toward Arafah does not.

Performing Umrah After Tawaf for Hajj
Ruling on performing Umrah after starting Hajj tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim performs Umrah after Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj and explain why a sacrifice (dam) is wajib.

Core Idea
Performing Umrah after starting Hajj actions is valid but requires a dam due to the irregular sequence.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim who has performed Tawaf al-Qudum (the welcome tawaf) and then enters ihram for Umrah, completing both. The Hanafi ruling is clear: the acts are valid, but a sacrifice is wajib to compensate for the improper ordering. The key insight lies in the principle that the later actions of Umrah are being performed on top of the earlier Hajj actions, which is not the prescribed sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: performing tawaf for Hajj (i.e. Tawaf al-Qudum), then entering ihram for Umrah, and completing both rites. The ruling: a sacrifice (dam) is wajib.
The ruling is not that the acts are invalid; they are valid but require compensation.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text states 'because he performed the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj.' This means the Umrah actions are superimposed on the Hajj actions, creating an irregular order that warrants a compensatory dam.
The proof is not a textual revelation but a rational explanation based on established fiqh principles.
3
Determine the legal implications
The irregular sequence does not affect the validity of either Hajj or Umrah; both are sahih. However, a wajib element (proper order) has been omitted, so a dam is due.
In Hanafi fiqh, missing a wajib (non-pillar) requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is that a dam is required regardless of intention. Some Shafi'is hold that a dam is only required if the irregularity was intentional. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the dam is wajib even if done unintentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن طافَ له، ثمّ أحرم بها فمضى عليهما ذبح فإن طاف له، ثمّ أحرم بها فمضى عليهما ذَبَح )؛ لأنه أتى بأفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج
If he performs tawaf for it (Hajj), then enters ihram for it ('Umrah), and proceeds with both, he must sacrifice. (If he performs tawaf for it, then enters ihram for it, and proceeds with both, he must sacrifice) because he performed the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The case is a person who has already performed the tawaf of Hajj (Tawaf al-Qudum) and then enters ihram for Umrah, completing both. The ruling is that a sacrifice (dam) is obligatory. The reason given is that the actions of Umrah are being superimposed upon the actions of Hajj, which is not the proper sequence and incurs a compensatory dam.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The welcome tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of performing Umrah after Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj according to the Hanafi school?
A) Both Hajj and Umrah are invalid.
B) No consequence; both are valid without penalty.
C) A sacrifice (dam) is required.
D) The Hajj becomes invalid but Umrah is valid.

Key Takeaway
When Umrah actions are performed after the initial Hajj tawaf, a dam (sacrifice) is wajib to compensate for the irregular sequence; the acts themselves remain valid.

Umrah During Hajj Days: Ruling and Make-Up
Ruling on a Hajji performing Umrah during the days of sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Hajji who initiates an Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or the Tashriq days, and explain why rafd, dam, and qada are required.

Core Idea
Umrah started during Hajj days binds but must be abandoned; make-up and sacrifice are wajib.

The Hajj days (Yawm al-Nahr and Tashriq) are reserved for the rites of Hajj. If a pilgrim who has already stood at Arafah enters ihram for Umrah during these days, a conflict arises: the Umrah is validly commenced and becomes binding, but performing its actions now would violate the proper sequence of Hajj. The Hanafi school rules that the pilgrim must abandon the Umrah (rafd), offer a sacrifice (dam), and later make up that Umrah (qada). This lesson unpacks that ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and act
The subject is a Muhrim (one already in Hajj) who, after standing at Arafah, declares ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or on the three days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th). Determine the precise timing and state of the pilgrim.
The pilgrim is already in Hajj ihram; the Umrah ihram is a second ihram.
2
Determine the initial hukm of the Umrah
According to the Hanafi school, entering ihram for Umrah—even on these days—makes the Umrah binding (lazimah). It is not invalid or prohibited; rather, it becomes an obligation that must be fulfilled or compensated.
Bindingness (luzum) arises from the act of commencement (shuru').
3
Analyze the conflict and the ruling of rafd
Because these days are designated for Hajj actions (stoning, stay at Mina, etc.), combining the actions of Umrah would entail karahah (dislike). To avoid that, the pilgrim must abandon (rafd) the Umrah. Rafd does not annul the obligation; it shifts it to compensation.
The reason (talil) is that the days are for Hajj, not Umrah.
4
Identify the consequences: dam and qada
Abandoning a binding Umrah requires a dam (sacrifice) as expiation and qada (make-up) performed later. The text explicitly states: 'he must abandon it, spill blood, and make it up.'
The dam is wajib; qada must be done at a later time.
5
Distil the practical outcome
Summarize: A Hajji who commences Umrah on these days must not continue the Umrah actions. He stays in Hajj, performs the Hajj completely, then after Hajj he must sacrifice one sheep/goat and later perform one Umrah to make up for the abandoned one.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن حج فأهل بعمرة يوم النحر، أو في ثلاثة تليه لزمته، ورُفِضَت وقضيت مع دم [١] قوله : فأهل بعمرة ؛ يعني المحرم بالحج فقط إذا وقف بعرفات ثم أحرم بالعمرة يوم النحر قبل الحلق أو بعده، وقبل طواف الزيارة، أو في الثلاثة المتصلة به؛ أي الحادي عشر والثاني عشر والثالث عشر، وهي أيام الرمي والمبيت بمنى، التزم الكراهة الجمع بين الإحرامين أو بين أعمالهما؛ فإنّ الأيام أيام أعمال الحج، لكنها تلزمه بالشروع، ويجب عليه أن يرفضها، وأراق الدم وقضاها. [٢] قوله : لزمته؛ جزاء لقوله : «إن حج»؛ أي لزمت تلك العمرة، حتى يلزم القضاء
And if he performs Hajj and then declares (ihram for) 'Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) or on the three days after it, it ('Umrah) becomes binding upon him, and it is abandoned and made up with a sacrifice. [1] His statement: 'He declares 'Umrah' means the Muhrim for Hajj only, after standing at Arafah, then enters ihram for 'Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr, before or after shaving, and before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, or on the three consecutive days after it (i.e., 11th, 12th, 13th, which are the days of stoning and staying at Mina); he incurs the dislike of combining the two ihrams or their actions, because those days are for the actions of Hajj, but it (the 'Umrah) becomes binding by commencement, and he must abandon it, spill blood (sacrifice), and make it up. [2] His statement: 'It becomes binding' is the result of his saying 'If he performs Hajj'; i.e., that 'Umrah becomes binding such that making it up is necessary.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding a person who is already in the state of Hajj (having stood at Arafah) and then enters ihram for Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice or the three following days (the days of Tashriq). The ruling is that the Umrah becomes binding (lazimah) by virtue of having commenced it, but because these days are designated for the actions of Hajj, the person must abandon (rafd) the Umrah, offer a sacrifice (dam), and later make up that Umrah. The commentary explains the reason: combining the actions of both Hajj and Umrah during the Hajj days is disliked, but since the Umrah was validly commenced, it must be completed in qada (make-up) after the Hajj.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandoning an ihram or ritual after having started it, in this context specifically the Umrah.
قضاء (qada): Making up or performing an act after its prescribed time, here the Umrah later.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as expiation for certain violations during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a Hajji do if he enters ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr?
A) Continue both Hajj and Umrah together.
B) Complete the Hajj and later make up the Umrah with a sacrifice.
C) The Umrah is invalid and no action is needed.
D) Only a sacrifice is required, no make-up.

Key Takeaway
An Umrah commenced during the Hajj days (Yawm al-Nahr and Tashriq) is valid and binding; the pilgrim must abandon its actions, offer a sacrifice, and perform a make-up Umrah later.

Definition and Obligations of Fai't al-Hajj
Defines fai't al-hajj and states the three wajib actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of fai't al-hajj and list the three wajib actions required of him.

Core Idea
A pilgrim who misses Arafah must abandon ihram, sacrifice, and make up Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine the case of a pilgrim who enters ihram for Hajj but, due to a miscalculation, arrives in Mecca after the Day of Arafah has passed. This person is called 'fai't al-hajj'. The Hanafi school outlines three specific obligations that become binding immediately. Understanding them ensures that the pilgrim does not remain in ihram improperly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Determine what qualifies a person as 'fai't al-hajj': one who entered ihram for Hajj from the miqat and missed the standing at Arafah due to a mistake in calculation or similar error.
2
State the three obligations
List the three wajib actions: rafd (abandon ihram by performing Umrah), qada (make up the missed Hajj), and dam (sacrifice an animal).
3
Note the hukm level
Recognize that all three are wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school, not merely recommended.
Wajib indicates a binding duty; omission without valid excuse incurs sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب دم فائت الحج أهلَ به أو بها، رفض، وقضى، وذبح [٣] قوله : فائت الحج؛ هو الذي أحرم بالحج من الميقات ودخل بمكة بعد انقضاء يوم عرفة لغلط في الحساب أو نحوه. [٤] قوله : يجب عليه هذا؛ أي التحلّل من الإحرام بأفعال العمرة، هو المنقول عن جمع من الصحابة، كما في «موطأ مالك»(۳)، وغيره. [٠] قوله : لصحة الشروع؛ علّة لقوله : «يقضي» يعني إنّما وجب القضاء لكون شروعه في الحج أو العمرة بالإحرام الثاني صحيحاً، فيلزمه، فإذا رفضه وجب قضاؤه، ويجب دم جبر لرفضه.
And a sacrifice is obligatory for the one who misses Hajj, whether he entered ihram for it (Hajj) or for her ('Umrah); he must abandon (the ihram), make up, and sacrifice. [3] His statement: 'The one who misses Hajj' is the one who entered ihram for Hajj from the miqat and entered Mecca after the passing of the Day of Arafah due to a mistake in calculation or the like. [4] His statement: 'This is obligatory upon him' means leaving the ihram through the actions of 'Umrah; this is transmitted from a group of Companions, as in the Muwatta of Malik and others. [0] His statement: 'Due to the validity of commencement' is the cause for his statement 'he makes up'; meaning, indeed, the make-up became obligatory because his commencement of Hajj or 'Umrah with the second ihram was valid, so it becomes binding upon him. When he abandons it, its make-up becomes obligatory, and a compensatory sacrifice is obligatory for his abandonment.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the actions of Companions for the 'fai't al-Hajj' — the one who misses the Hajj because he arrives at Mecca after the time of standing at Arafah has passed, often due to miscalculation. The obligation is threefold: he must abandon his current ihram (rafd), then perform the actions of 'Umrah to exit ihram (tahallul), sacrifice a dam, and subsequently make up (qada) the Hajj (or Umrah, if that is what he missed) at another time. The proof cited is the practice of Companions as recorded in the Muwatta of Imam Malik. The commentary explains that since the commencement of the ihram was valid, it must be either completed (which is impossible for Hajj after the time) or abandoned with compensation. Thus, make-up becomes wajib.

Key Terms
فائت الحج (fai't al-hajj): A person who entered ihram for Hajj but missed the standing at Arafah due to timing error.
تحلل (tahallul): Leaving the state of ihram, usually by performing Umrah actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wait until next year and resume ihram.
B) Perform the actions of Umrah (tawaf, sa'i, shaving).
C) Offer a sacrifice only.
D) Cut hair and nails.

Key Takeaway
A pilgrim who misses Arafah must perform Umrah to exit ihram, sacrifice an animal, and make up the missed Hajj at a later time.

Proof and Rationale for the Fai't al-Hajj Ruling
Explains the proof and cause for the obligations on fai't al-hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proof (dalil) for the obligations on fai't al-hajj and explain the cause (illa) for qada.

Core Idea
The obligations derive from Companion practice, and qada is wajib because the original ihram was valid.

Having learned the obligations, we now examine the proof. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Prophet's Companions as transmitted in Muwatta Malik. Additionally, the commentator explains that make-up is required because the initial entry into ihram was valid—therefore it must be completed or compensated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dalil
The text cites the practice of a group of Companions (qawl sahabi) as recorded in Muwatta Malik. This is the primary proof for the obligations.
Qawl sahabi is a recognized source of law in Hanafi usul.
2
Assess the epistemological weight
The transmission is considered zanni (speculative) in thubut but the meaning is qati (definitive) because the actions of the Companions are clear.
Zanni thubut means the chain is not mutawatir; but the ruling is strong due to multiple transmissions.
3
Analyze the cause for qada
The text states: 'li sihhat al-shuru' (due to the validity of commencement). Because the pilgrim's ihram was valid upon entering, it creates an obligation that must be fulfilled either by completing the Hajj (impossible) or by making it up.
This cause (illa) shows that qada is not arbitrary but tied to the validity of the original act.
4
Connect to the overall ruling
The same cause explains why dam is required: it compensates for the abandonment of the valid ihram.

Source Text

[٤] قوله : يجب عليه هذا؛ أي التحلّل من الإحرام بأفعال العمرة، هو المنقول عن جمع من الصحابة، كما في «موطأ مالك»(۳)، وغيره. And a sacrifice is obligatory for the one who misses Hajj, whether he entered ihram for it (Hajj) or for her ('Umrah); he must abandon (the ihram), make up, and sacrifice. [3] His statement: 'The one who misses Hajj' is the one who entered ihram for Hajj from the miqat and entered Mecca after the passing of the Day of Arafah due to a mistake in calculation or the like. Adding a Second Ihram During Hajj Days and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Transformation
Explains the obligation to abandon a second ihram and offer a sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for adding a second ihram during Hajj days and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on the transformation of ihram for the Faa'it al-Hajj.

Core Idea
A second ihram during Hajj days is valid but must be abandoned with a sacrifice; for the one who missed Hajj, his ihram does not transform into Umrah.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim who, while already in ihram for Hajj, assumes another ihram for Umrah during the days of sacrifice. The passage explains that this second ihram is legally binding (valid) but must be abandoned (rafd) and compensated with a dam. It then addresses the special case of the one who missed Hajj (Faa'it al-Hajj) and the intra-Hanafi dispute: does his ihram transform into Umrah? The relied-upon position is that it does not transform, per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
A person in ihram for Hajj assumes a second ihram for Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice or the three days following. This is the act under discussion.
2
Determine the ruling for the second ihram
The second ihram is binding (valid) because the act of entering ihram is sahih. However, combining two ihrams during this period is prohibited, so the second must be abandoned (rafd) and made up (qada) with a blood offering (dam).
The ruling: the second ihram is sahih but requires rafd and dam.
3
Analyze the dispute for the Faa'it al-Hajj
For the one who missed Hajj (failed to stand at Arafat), he must exit ihram by performing Umrah acts. If he then assumes another ihram, he becomes a combiner of two ihrams of the same type and must abandon the second. The text discusses whether his original Hajj ihram transforms into Umrah ihram.
4
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the ihram does not transform; he remains in Hajj ihram and merely performs Umrah acts to exit. Abu Yusuf holds that it transforms into Umrah ihram. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the majority.
The thamarah: if transformation occurs, no separate Umrah is needed; if not, he remains in Hajj ihram and his actions are a means to exit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن حج فأهل بعمرة يوم النحر، أو في ثلاثة تليه لزمته، ورفضت وقضيت مع دم، ويجب دم فائت الحج أهل به أو بها، رفض، وقضى، وذبح. أي إنما لزمته؛ لأن الجمع بين إحرامي الحج والعمرة صحيح. ويجب دم فائت الحج إذا أحرم بحج أو عمرة، يجب أن يرفض الإحرام، ويتحلل بأفعال العمرة؛ لأن فائت الحج يجب عليه هذا، ثم يقضي ما أحرم به لصحة الشروع ويذبح. وإنما يرفض إحرام الحج؛ لأنه يصير جامعاً بين إحرامي الحج، فيرفض الثاني. وإنما يرفض إحرام العمرة؛ لأنه تجب عليه عمرة لفوات الحج، فيصير بالإحرام جامعاً بين العمرتين، فيرفض الثانية. وإنما يجب عليه دم؛ للتحلل قبل أوانه بالرفض. ولم يقل بين إحرامي العمرة؛ لأن إحرام فائت الحج لا ينقلب إحراماً للعمرة، بل هو محرم بالحج الآن كما كان، وإنما يجب عليه الإتيان بأفعال العمرة، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف ينقلب إحرامه إحرام العمرة.
If he performs Hajj and then assumes ihram for Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice, or in the three days following it, it becomes binding upon him, and it is abandoned and made up with a blood offering. And a blood offering is obligatory for the one who missed Hajj if he assumed ihram for Hajj or Umrah: he abandons, makes up, and slaughters. That is, it becomes binding upon him because combining the two ihrams of Hajj and Umrah is valid. And a blood offering is obligatory for the one who missed Hajj if he assumes ihram for Hajj or Umrah: he must abandon the ihram and exit by the acts of Umrah because the one who missed Hajj must do this, then he makes up what he assumed ihram for due to the validity of the commencement, and slaughters. And he abandons the ihram of Hajj because he becomes a combiner of two ihrams of Hajj, so he abandons the second. And he abandons the ihram of Umrah because an Umrah is obligatory upon him due to the loss of Hajj, so by assuming ihram he becomes a combiner between two Umrahs, so he abandons the second. And a blood offering is obligatory upon him because of exiting before its proper time by abandonment. And he did not say 'between the two ihrams of Umrah' because the ihram of the one who missed Hajj does not transform into an ihram for Umrah; rather, he is in ihram for Hajj now as he was, and he is only required to perform the acts of Umrah. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf, his ihram transforms into an ihram for Umrah.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with two scenarios: (1) a person in ihram for Hajj who adds a second ihram for Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice or the three days after, and (2) a person who missed Hajj (Faa'it al-Hajj) and then assumes a second ihram. In both cases, the second ihram is valid but must be abandoned (rafd) because combining two conflicting sets of rites during the days of Hajj is prohibited. The person must make up the abandoned ihram later and offer a sacrifice (dam) for the premature dissolution. The text explains why the second ihram is binding: because the act of entering ihram is valid (sahih) and thus creates obligations. For the one who missed Hajj, he must perform Umrah acts to exit ihram; if he then assumes another ihram (for Hajj or Umrah), he becomes a combiner and must abandon the second one. The text also discusses an intra-Hanafi difference: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the ihram of the one who missed Hajj does not transform into Umrah; he remains in his original Hajj ihram and merely performs Umrah acts to exit. However, Abu Yusuf holds that it transforms into an ihram for Umrah. The relied-upon position is the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The blood offering is required because the abandonment (rafd) is a premature exit from ihram, which is a violation requiring compensation.

Key Terms
رفض (rafḍ): Abandonment of an ihram before completing its rites, which requires compensation (dam) and making up (qada).
فائت الحج (fāʼit al-ḥajj): A person who missed the standing at Arafat (wuquf) thus fails to complete Hajj and must exit ihram by performing Umrah acts and later make up the Hajj.
دم جبر (dam jabr): A blood offering (sacrificial animal) required to compensate for a deficiency or violation during Hajj/Umrah, such as premature exit from ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person performing Hajj who then assumes ihram for Umrah on the Day of Sacrifice?
A) The Umrah is invalid and must be ignored.
B) The Umrah is binding but must be abandoned and made up with a sacrifice.
C) He may continue with both Hajj and Umrah together.
D) He must abandon his Hajj and complete the Umrah instead.

Key Takeaway
A second ihram during Hajj days is valid but must be abandoned with a sacrifice; for the one who missed Hajj, his ihram does not transform into Umrah according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

6 min
The Ruling on Rejecting a Second Ihram: The Non-Transformation of Ihram
Explaining the rejection of a second ihram and the intra-Hanafi dispute on transformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a second ihram is rejected in the case of a missed Hajj, explain the Hanafi position on the non-transformation of the original ihram, and apply the analogy of the masbuq to similar cases.

Core Idea
A second ihram is rejected because it creates an impermissible combination; the original ihram does not transform into an Umrah ihram.

This passage expands on a ruling about a person who, having missed the original Hajj, enters into a second ihram. The commentator explains the reasoning behind rejecting the second ihram and highlights a dispute within the Hanafi school: whether the original Hajj ihram transforms into an Umrah ihram when the person performs Umrah actions. We will examine the ruling, the analogy to the latecomer in prayer, and the practical implications of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: a person missed Hajj (fawt al-hajj) and is now performing Umrah actions. He then enters a second ihram, either for Hajj or Umrah. The ruling: the second ihram is rejected (rafḍ) and a dam (blood penalty) is required.
The rejection occurs because combining two ihrams for the same ritual is not legislated.
2
Understand the reasoning based on combination (jam‘)
Adding a second ihram creates a combination of two ihrams for the same ritual – two Hajj ihrams or two Umrah ihrams. Since this is not legislated, the second must be annulled.
The text explicitly says: 'inna bimā thumma yasīru jāmi‘an bayna iḥrāmay al-ḥajj' – he becomes combining between two ihrams of Hajj.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on transformation
According to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), the original ihram does not transform into an Umrah ihram. The person remains in Hajj ihram while performing Umrah actions. This is analogous to a masbuq (latecomer in prayer) who is a follower in the original takbeer but recites individually for missed rak‘ahs. According to an alternate view from Abū Yūsuf, the ihram does transform.
The dispute is whether the original Hajj ihram changes its character when the person performs Umrah actions.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the ihram does not transform, then adding a second Hajj ihram would combine two Hajj ihrams; if it does transform, then adding a second Umrah ihram would combine two Umrah ihrams. In either case, the second ihram is rejected. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is the view of the two that the ihram does not transform.
The practical difference is minimal in this case because both views lead to rejection of the second ihram, but the underlying principle differs.
5
Apply the analogy of the masbuq to the far‘
The commentator explicitly compares the one who missed Hajj to a masbuq: just as the masbuq is a follower in the original takbeer but recites individually for missed rak‘ahs, similarly the person who missed Hajj remains in the state of Hajj ihram (the original takbeer) but performs Umrah actions individually. This supports the view that the original ihram does not transform.
This is a qiyās jaliyy (clear analogy) based on the shared ‘illah of remaining within the original framework while performing substitute actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما يَرْفَضُ إحرام الحج ؛ لأنه يصير جامعاً بين إحرامي الحج، فيرفض وإنما يرفض إحرام العمرة ؛ لأنَّه تجب عليه عمرة ؛ لفواتِ الحج، فيصير بالإحرام جامعاً بين العمرتين ، فيرفض الثانية. وإنما يجب عليه دم ؛ للتحلل قبل أوانه بالرفض. [1]قوله : بين إحرامي الحج ؛ فإن إحرام الحج الأوّل باق لا يتحلّل منه إلا بأفعال العمرة، فإذا أحرم ثانياً بالحج صارَ جامعاً بين الإحرامين للحج، وهو غير مشروع ، فيجب عليه نقض الثاني. [٢) قوله : لفوات الحج ؛ لما مر من أن فائت الحج يجب عليه التحلّل بأفعال العمرة. [٣] قوله : جامعاً ؛ قال في «النهاية»: بيانه : أنّ الركن الأصلي في الحج هو الوقوف، فإذا فاته فعليه أن يتحلّل بأفعال العمرة، فنقول : فائت الحج محرم بإحرام الحج مباشر لأفعال العمرة، بمنزلة المسبوق إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق، فإنّه مقتد في أصل التحريمة، حتى لا يصح الاقتداء به منفردا في الأعمال، فتلزمه القراءة، فإذا أحرم لعمرة كان جامعاً بين العمرتين ، وإذا أحرم بحجة صار جامعاً بين الحجتين. (٤) قوله : بين العمرتين؛ لم يقل بين إحرامي العمرة ؛ لأن إحرام فائت الحج لا ينقلب إحراماً للعمرة، بل هو محرم بالحج الآن كما كان، وإنما يجب عليه الإتيان بأفعال العمرة، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف [؟] ينقلب إحرامه إحرام العمرة.
And the ihram of Hajj is rejected because he becomes combining between two ihrams of Hajj, so it is rejected. And the ihram of Umrah is rejected because an Umrah becomes obligatory on him due to missing of Hajj, so by the ihram he becomes combining between two Umrahs, so the second is rejected. And a penalty of dam is obligatory on him because he becomes halal before its time by rejection. [1] His saying: 'between two ihrams of Hajj' – because the first ihram of Hajj remains, he cannot exit from it except by the actions of Umrah. So if he enters ihram again for Hajj, he becomes combining between two ihrams for Hajj, which is not legislated, so he must annul the second. [2] His saying: 'due to missing of Hajj' – as previously stated that one who misses Hajj must exit by the actions of Umrah. [3] His saying: 'combining' – said in al-Nihayah: its explanation: the essential pillar of Hajj is the standing at Arafat. So if he misses it, he must exit by the actions of Umrah. So we say: the one who missed Hajj is in the ihram of Hajj performing the actions of Umrah, like the latecomer when he stands to make up what he missed; he is a follower in the original takbeer, so that following him as an individual in actions is not valid, and recitation is obligatory on him. So if he entered ihram for Umrah, he becomes combining between two Umrahs, and if he entered ihram for Hajj, he becomes combining between two Hajjs. (4) His saying: 'between two Umrahs' – he did not say between two ihrams of Umrah because the ihram of the one who missed Hajj does not transform into the ihram of Umrah, rather he is in the state of ihram for Hajj now as he was, and he is only obligated to perform the actions of Umrah. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to Abu Yusuf [؟] his ihram transforms into the ihram of Umrah.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on a ruling about a person who, after missing the original Hajj, enters into a second ihram. The text explains why the second ihram is rejected: because it creates an impermissible combination of either two Hajj ihrams or two Umrah ihrams. The commentator gives analogies: the person is like a latecomer (masbuq) in prayer who must follow the imam in the original takbeer but recites individually for missed rak'ahs. The commentary also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the original ihram for Hajj does not transform into an Umrah ihram; rather the person remains in the state of ihram for Hajj while performing Umrah actions. However, the text as given states that according to Abu Yusuf, his ihram transforms into that of Umrah, but due to OCR corruption, this is uncertain.

Key Terms
رفض (rafḍ): Annulment or cancellation of the second ihram because it is impermissible.
مسبوق (masbūq): A latecomer to congregational prayer who misses one or more rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the second ihram rejected in this situation?
A) Because it creates a combination of two Hajjs or two Umrahs
B) Because the person's original ihram is invalid
C) Because he did not have the intention
D) Because he missed the deadline

Key Takeaway
The second ihram is always rejected when a person is already in a valid ihram for the missed Hajj, regardless of the dispute on transformation, and a dam is required.

Definition and Scope of Ihsaar in the Hanafi School
Definition of ihsaar and dispute over its causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ihsaar, distinguish it from the opposing view that restricts it to enemy prevention, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving illness or loss of provisions.

Core Idea
Ihsaar includes any prevention—enemy, illness, or lost provisions—because the Quran's word is general, not limited to its occasion.

The chapter on Ihsaar addresses what happens when a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah. This lesson focuses on the opening passage, which defines ihsaar and immediately presents a key dispute: does it only apply when an enemy blocks the way, or does it cover any obstacle? The Hanafi school adopts the broader view, and we will explore the evidence and reasoning behind that position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Pinpoint the core question: Is ihsaar restricted to prevention by an enemy (as some scholars hold) or does it include any cause such as illness, loss of provisions, etc.?
The passage states: 'Ikhtalafa fih' (there is disagreement).
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi school says ihsaar occurs by any prevention. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse 'fa in uhsirtum' which uses a general word, and the hadith 'man kasara aw 'araja faqad halla' (whoever breaks a bone or limps has become halal).
The commentator says 'indana al-ihsar yakun bi kull ma yamna' (according to us, ihsaar is by anything that prevents).
3
State the opposing position and its evidence
The opposing view restricts ihsaar to a disbelieving enemy. They rely on the specific occasion of revelation (sabab al-nuzul) when the Prophet was prevented by the Quraysh at Hudaybiyyah.
The passage says 'qila innahu mukhtass bi ma idha mana' al-‘aduw al-kafir' (it is said it is specific to a disbelieving enemy).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the legal consideration ('ibrah) is the generality of the wording ('umum al-lafz), not the specificity of the occasion (husus al-sabab). The verse uses a general term 'uhsirtum' so it applies to all forms of prevention.
The commentator cites 'al-'ibrah li 'umum al-lafz wa itlaqihi, la li khusus mawridihi'.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under the narrow view, a pilgrim prevented by illness would not be considered muhsar and would not have the same ruling of sending a sacrifice and becoming halal. Under the Hanafi view, they would.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the dispute).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحصار
إن أُحْصِرَ المحرم بعدو أو مرض بعث المفرد دماً، والقارنُ دمين، وعين يوماً يذبح فيه، ولو قبل يوم النحر
[1]قوله : باب الإحصار ؛ هو لغة : المنع ، وشرعاً : منع المحرم من الحج أو العمرة بأن يحول بينه وبين النُّسُكِ ما لا يمكن به أن يؤدّيه، ولما كان هذا من العوارض النادرة ، أخر ذكره.
[٢] قوله : بعدو أو مرض : ؛ اختلف فيه :
فقيل : إنّه مختص بما إذا منع العدو الكافر ؛ لقوله تعالى: وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ فَإِنْ أُحْصِرْتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيَ وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُهُ وسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الهَدَى يَحِلَّهُ )، نزلت حين خرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع أصحابه محترمين بالعمرة سنة ست من الهجرة، فمنعهم الكفار عن دخول مكة وأحصروهم بالحديبية. وعندنا : الإحصار يكون بكل ما يمنع، كالمرض وهلاكِ النفقة، وموت المحرم أو الزوج للمرأة، ونحو ذلك، فإنّ العبرة لعموم اللفظ وإطلاقه، لا لخصوص مورده ، ويشهده حديث: «من كسر أو عرج فقد حل، وعليه حجة أخرى)، أخرجه أصحاب السنن وغيرهم، وفي المقام تفصيل فرغنا عنه في «التعليق الممجّد على موطأ الإمام محمد (۳) قوله : بعث ؛ أي إذا أحصر خارج الحرم، فإن أحصر في الحرم يذبحه مكانه.
[٤]قوله : المفرد ؛ أي الذي أحرم بالحج منفرداً فامتنع. [0] قوله : وعين ... الخ ؛ يعني يبعث المحرم هدياً إلى الحرم مع رجل ويعين له يوماً
Chapter on Ihsaar. If the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or illness, the one performing Hajj only (mufrid) sends a blood sacrifice, the one performing Qiran sends two blood sacrifices, and he appoints a day on which to slaughter, even if before the Day of Nahr. [1] His saying: 'Chapter on Ihsaar' – it is linguistically prevention, and legally: preventing the muhrim from Hajj or Umrah by something that comes between him and the ritual that he cannot perform it. And since this is from rare occurrences, he delayed its mention. [2] His saying: 'by enemy or illness' – there is disagreement about it: some said it is specific to when a disbelieving enemy prevents because of His saying: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, and if you are prevented, then whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal, and do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place.' It was revealed when the Prophet ﷺ went out with his companions in the state of ihram for Umrah in the year 6 AH, and the disbelievers prevented them from entering Makkah and blockaded them at Hudaybiyyah. According to us: prevention occurs by anything that prevents, like illness, loss of provisions, death of the muhrim or the husband of a woman, and so on, because consideration is given to the generality of the word and its absolute nature, not to the specificity of its occasion. And this is witnessed by the hadith: 'Whoever breaks a bone or limps, he has become halal, and he owes another Hajj' – narrated by the authors of Sunan and others. And there is detail in this regard which we have completed in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad on the Muwatta' of Imam Muhammad. [3] His saying: 'sends' – i.e., if he is prevented outside the Haram, then if he is prevented inside the Haram, he slaughters it in its place. [4] His saying: 'the mufrid' – i.e., the one who entered ihram for Hajj alone and was prevented. [0] His saying: 'and appoints...' etc. – means the muhrim sends the sacrificial animal to the Haram with a man and appoints for him a day.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Ihsaar (prevention from completing pilgrimage). The commentator first gives the linguistic and legal definition: any hindrance that prevents the pilgrim from continuing the rites. He notes that the chapter is placed late in the book because it deals with rare issues. Then he addresses the apparent limitation in the matn to 'enemy or illness' and presents a dispute: some restrict ihsaar to an enemy, basing it on the verse from Surah al-Baqarah revealed at Hudaybiyyah. The Hanafi position, however, is that ihsaar applies to any prevention, including illness, loss of provisions, death of the pilgrim or the husband, etc., because the general application of the word is considered, not the specific occasion of revelation. The hadith of one who breaks a bone or limps supports this broad view. The passage then briefly explains the phrase 'sends' and 'mufrid' and the appointment of a day.

Key Terms
إحصار (iḥṣār): Prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah by an obstacle.
محرم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
عبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب (al-'ibrah bi 'umum al-lafz la bi khusus al-sabab): A usul principle: legal consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not the specific occasion of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid cause of ihsaar?
A) Only enemy blockade
B) Enemy blockade and illness only
C) Any prevention, including illness, loss of provisions, and enemy
D) Only natural disasters

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ihsaar broadly as any prevention from completing pilgrimage, based on the general wording of the Quran and supporting hadith.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Rulings of Ihsaar (Prevention) in Hajj and Umrah
Explains the definition, causes, and rulings of being prevented during Hajj/Umrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Ihsaar, apply the rulings for sending the Hadi, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing, and identify the make-up obligations.

Core Idea
Ihsaar covers any prevention; the Hadi must be sent to the Haram; Abu Hanifa allows slaughter any day; make-up is required.

This passage from Al-Hidayah unpacks the chapter on Ihsaar, a rare but important topic. It first defines Ihsaar, then resolves a key scope dispute: does prevention require an enemy? Hanafis say no, based on general wording. It then details the compensation—one Hadi for Mufrid, two for Qarin—and the rules for timing, place, and release. A well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether slaughter for Hajj prevention must be on Yawm al-Nahr is discussed, with Abu Hanifa's view being the relied-upon position. Finally, it outlines the make-up pilgrimage obligations.

Guided Path
1
Define Ihsaar and understand its scope
Learn the linguistic and legal definitions. Note the dispute: some restrict to enemy; Hanafis include any prevention due to general wording. The hadith 'man kusira aw 'arija' supports this.
This is a classic application of the usul principle: al-ibrah bi umum al-lafz.
2
Determine the compensation and procedure
Identify: Mufrid sends 1 Hadi, Qarin sends 2. The Hadi must be sent to the Haram with a designated day for slaughter. Release occurs upon slaughter, not upon shaving (shaving is sunnah).
The slaughter must occur inside the Haram.
3
Analyze the timing dispute
Abu Hanifa allows slaughter any day; the Sahibayn restrict to Yawm al-Nahr for Hajj. Abu Hanifa analogizes to other expiatory blood (not time-specific). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
For Umrah, all agree any day is fine.
4
Identify the make-up obligations
After release, the Muhrim must make up the missed pilgrimage: if prevented from Hajj, a Hajj and Umrah; from Umrah, an Umrah; from Qiran, a Hajj and two Umrahs (according to Abu Hanifa).
This ensures that the original obligation is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحصار
إن أُحْصِرَ المحرم بعدو أو مرض بعث المفرد دماً، والقارنُ دمين، وعين يوماً يذبح فيه، ولو قبل يوم النحر
قوله : باب الإحصار ؛ هو لغة : المنع ، وشرعاً : منع المحرم من الحج أو العمرة بأن يحول بينه وبين النُّسُكِ ما لا يمكن به أن يؤدّيه، ولما كان هذا من العوارض النادرة، أخر ذكره.
قوله : بعدو أو مرض : اختلف فيه : فقيل : إنّه مختص بما إذا منع العدو الكافر ؛ لقوله تعالى: {فإن أحصرتم فما استيسر من الهدي} نزلت حين خرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع أصحابه محترمين بالعمرة سنة ست من الهجرة، فمنعهم الكفار عن دخول مكة وأحصروهم بالحديبية. وعندنا : الإحصار يكون بكل ما يمنع، كالمرض وهلاك النفقة، وموت المحرم أو الزوج للمرأة، ونحو ذلك، فإنّ العبرة لعموم اللفظ وإطلاقه، لا لخصوص مورده، ويشهده حديث: «من كسر أو عرج فقد حل، وعليه حجة أخرى» أخرجه أصحاب السنن وغيرهم.
قوله : بعث ؛ أي إذا أحصر خارج الحرم، فإن أحصر في الحرم يذبحه مكانه.
قوله : المفرد ؛ أي الذي أحرم بالحج منفرداً فامتنع.
قوله : وعين ... الخ ؛ يعني يبعث المحرم هدياً إلى الحرم مع رجل ويعين له يوماً للذبح، ويأمره أن يذبح في الحرم في ذلك اليوم، فإذا وصل ذلك اليوم والوقت تحلّل من إحرامه في موضع حصره.
وفي حل لا، وبذبحه يحل قبل حلق وتقصير، وعليه إن حل من حج حج وعمرة، ومن عمرة عمرة، ومن قران حج وعمرتان هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وأما عندهما، فإن كان محصراً بالعمرة فكذا، وإن كان محصراً بالحج لا يجوز الذبح إلا في يوم النحر
قوله : فكذا ؛ أي يُعين له يوماً : أي يوم كان، فإن ذبح هدي العمرة لا يختص بيوم النحر اتفاقاً.
قوله : إلا في يوم النحر ؛ لأنّ ذبحه مختص بالزمان المعين كاختصاصه بالمكان المعين.
وله : أن هذا الهدي دم كفّارة، فيختص بالمكان دون الزمان، كسائر دماء الكفارات.
قوله : وفي حل لا ؛ أي يجب أن يذبح ذلك في الحرم لا في خارج الحرم ؛ لقوله تعالى: {حتى يبلغ الهدي محله} مع قوله تعالى: {ثم محلّها إلى البيت العتيق}.
قوله : قبل حلق ؛ يعني لا يجب شيء من ذلك، بل يقع التحلّل بنفس الذبح، نعم يسن أن يفعل أحدهما كما فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه عام الحديبية.
قوله : عمرة ؛ قضاء لما فات منه، وكذا يجب الحج للمحصر من الحج قضاء، وأما وجوب العمرة عليه فلكونه في معنى فائت الحج.
Chapter of Ihsaar (Prevention). If a Muhrim (one in Ihram) is prevented by an enemy or illness, the one performing Ifrad (Hajj only) sends one animal (Dam), the Qarin (performing Qiran) sends two animals, and he specifies a day on which it will be slaughtered, even if before the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). (Commentary) His saying: Chapter of Ihsaar: Linguistically: prevention. Legally: preventing the Muhrim from Hajj or Umrah by something that interposes between him and the ritual such that he cannot perform it. Since this is among rare occurrences, its mention is delayed. His saying: by an enemy or illness: there is disagreement: some say it is specific to prevention by a disbelieving enemy due to His saying {But if you are prevented, then [send] what is easy of the sacrificial animal} which was revealed when the Prophet ﷺ went out with his companions in the state of Ihram for Umrah in year 6 AH, and the disbelievers prevented them from entering Makkah and blockaded them at Hudaybiyyah. According to us: Ihsaar occurs by anything that prevents, like illness, loss of provisions, death of the Muhrim or the husband of a woman, and the like, for consideration is given to the generality of the wording and its absoluteness, not to the specificity of its context. This is witnessed by the hadith: 'Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame has become Halal (released from Ihram) and he must perform another Hajj,' narrated by the authors of Sunan and others. His saying: 'sends' means if he is prevented outside the Haram; if he is prevented inside the Haram, he slaughters it in its place. His saying: 'the Mufrid' (one performing Ifrad) means one who entered Ihram for Hajj alone and was then prevented. His saying: 'and specifies...' means the Muhrim sends a Hadi (sacrificial animal) to the Haram with a man and specifies for him a day for slaughter, and orders him to slaughter it in the Haram on that day. When that day and time arrives, he becomes free of his Ihram in his place of prevention. (End of matn continuation) [And the ruling: it must be] within the Haram, not outside; and by its slaughter he becomes free before shaving and trimming. And he is required: if he becomes free from Hajj, he must perform Hajj and Umrah; from Umrah, an Umrah; from Qiran, Hajj and two Umrahs. This according to Abu Hanifa رحمه الله. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he is prevented in Umrah, it is the same; but if he is prevented in Hajj, slaughter is not permitted except on the Day of Nahr. (Commentary) His saying: 'it is the same' means he specifies a day: any day, for slaughter of the Hadi of Umrah is not restricted to the Day of Nahr by agreement. His saying: 'except on the Day of Nahr' because its slaughter is specific to a fixed time just as it is specific to a fixed place. And Abu Hanifa's view: this Hadi is an expiatory blood (Dam Kaffarah), so it is specific to place but not time, like all expiatory bloods. His saying: 'within the Haram, not outside' means it must be slaughtered in the Haram, not outside it, due to His saying {until the Hadi reaches its place of sacrifice} together with His saying {then their place is at the Ancient House}. His saying: 'before shaving' means nothing of that is obligatory; rather, release occurs by the slaughter itself, but it is Sunnah to do one of them as the Messenger ﷺ and his companions did in the year of Hudaybiyyah. His saying: 'Umrah' as a make-up for what was missed; likewise, Hajj is obligatory for the one prevented from Hajj as a make-up. As for the obligation of Umrah upon him, it is because he is akin to one who missed Hajj.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of Ihsaar (prevention) from Al-Hidayah. It begins by defining Ihsaar linguistically and legally. The commentator clarifies the scope of causes: a minority view restricts it to enemy action, citing the specific incident of Hudaybiyyah. The Hanafi position, however, takes the general wording of the Quranic verse, accepting any prevention—illness, loss of means, death of the Muhrim or spouse. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ ruled that a broken bone or lameness releases one from Ihram. Then the rulings: the Mufrid (one in Hajj only) sends one animal, the Qarin sends two. He must specify a day for slaughter, even before the Day of Nahr, according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict this: for Umrah prevention, any day is fine; for Hajj prevention, slaughter only on the Day of Nahr. The commentator explains Abu Hanifa's analogy: this is an expiatory blood (Dam), which is tied to the sanctity of the place (Haram) but not a specific time, unlike other rituals. The slaughter must occur inside the Haram, based on Quranic verses. Release from Ihram occurs upon slaughter, without the need for shaving or trimming (though it is Sunnah). Finally, the Muhrim must make up the missed pilgrimage: if prevented from Hajj, a Hajj and an Umrah; from Umrah, an Umrah; from Qiran, a Hajj and two Umrahs. This is the view of Abu Hanifa, while the companions agree on the Umrah case but differ on Hajj.

Key Terms
الإحصار (al-ihsaar): Prevention of a Muhrim from completing Hajj or Umrah by an external obstacle.
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram as a compensation for being prevented.
دم (dam): Blood; here refers to the expiatory animal sacrifice required for Ihsaar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when can the Hadi be slaughtered for a person prevented from Hajj?
A) Only on the Day of Nahr
B) Any day, even before the Day of Nahr
C) Only within the Haram on the Day of Nahr
D) Only after the 10th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Ihsaar includes any prevention; the Hadi must be sent to the Haram; release occurs by slaughter; make-up is required.

Place of Hady Slaughter and Qada for Muhsar
Ruling on where to slaughter and compensation upon release from ihsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on where the muhsar must slaughter the hady and determine the qada obligations for different types of ihram (Hajj, Umrah, Qiran).

Core Idea
Slaughter in the Haram is wajib; release occurs by slaughter alone; shaving is Sunnah, not a condition.

One of the essential rulings for a person prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj or Umrah is knowing where to slaughter the hady and how to properly exit ihram. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that the sacrifice must be made within the Haram, not outside, citing explicit Quranic verses. It also explains that the muhsar becomes halal by the act of slaughter itself—shaving or trimming hair is recommended but not obligatory. Additionally, after the obstacle is removed, the muhsar must make up the missed rituals (qada).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled on and its hukm level. The passage rules on where the muhsar must slaughter the hady and the obligations upon release.
The core act is slaughtering the hady; the ruling is that it must be done in the Haram (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited for the ruling. The author quotes two Quranic verses: 2:196 and 22:33.
The dalil is naqli (Quran).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verses prove the ruling. The first links shaving to the hady reaching its place; the second specifies that place as the Ancient House (Kaaba). Together they indicate that slaughter must be in the Haram.
The imperative 'do not shave until...' implies that the hady must first reach its designated location.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on shaving
Recognize that there is a difference of opinion on whether shaving is required for tahlil. The text states that slaughter alone suffices; shaving is only Sunnah, not wajib.
Some other schools hold shaving to be obligatory. The Hanafi position is based on the Prophet's practice at Hudaybiyyah.
5
Apply the qada rules
Understand the compensation (qada) required after release. If the muhsar was in Hajj, he must later perform Hajj and Umrah; if in Umrah, one Umrah; if in Qiran, Hajj and two Umrahs.
The obligation of qada is wajib upon removal of the obstacle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حل لا، وبذبحه يحل قبل حلق وتقصير ، وعليه إن حل من حج حج وعمرة، ومن عمرة عمرة، ومن قران حج وعمرتان.
قوله : وفي حل لا ; أي يجب أن يذبح ذلك في الحرم لا في خارج الحرم ; لقوله تعالى: وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحِلَّهُ (البقرة: 196) مع قوله تعالى: ثُمَّ مَحِلُّهَا إِلَى الْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ (الحج: 33). قوله : قبل حلق ; يعني لا يجب شيء من ذلك، بل يقع التحلّل بنفس الذبح، نعم يسن أن يفعل أحدهما كما فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه عام الحديبية. قوله : عمرة ; قضاء لما فات منه، وكذا يجب الحج للمحصر من الحج قضاء، وأما وجوب العمرة عليه فلكونه في معنى فائت الحج.
And regarding 'not permissible outside the Haram': he becomes halal by slaughtering before shaving and trimming. And upon him, if he is released from Hajj, (he must perform) Hajj and Umrah; from Umrah, one Umrah; from Qiran, Hajj and two Umrahs. He said: 'And regarding not permissible outside': meaning it is obligatory to slaughter that in the Haram, not outside the Haram, due to His statement: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place of sacrifice' (2:196) along with His statement: 'Then their place of sacrifice is at the Ancient House' (22:33). He said: 'before shaving': meaning nothing of that is obligatory; rather tahlil occurs by the slaughter itself. Yes, it is Sunnah to do one of them as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his Companions did in the year of Hudaybiyyah. He said: 'Umrah': as compensation for what was missed; similarly, Hajj is obligatory for the one prevented from Hajj as compensation. As for the obligation of Umrah upon him, it is because he is in the position of one who missed Hajj.
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the actions of one who is prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj or Umrah. The author states that the muhsar must send a hady (sacrificial animal) to the Haram and slaughter it there; slaughtering outside the Haram is not valid. The proof is from the Quranic verses commanding that the hady reaches its place before shaving, and that the place of sacrifice is the Ancient House (the Kaaba). The commentator clarifies that the muhsar becomes halal (released from ihram) by the act of slaughter itself; shaving or trimming hair is not a condition but is recommended (Sunnah), following the example of the Prophet at Hudaybiyyah. If the muhsar is released from a Hajj ihram, he must later make up for it by performing both Hajj and Umrah (qada). If he was in Umrah, he makes up one Umrah. If he was in Qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah), he makes up both Hajj and two Umrahs. The reason is that the missed ritual must be compensated, and the obligation of Umrah for one prevented from Hajj is analogized to a missed Hajj.

Key Terms
الإحصار (al-ihsar): Prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an external obstacle such as enemy, sickness, or other force.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhsar to allow release from ihram.
القضاء (al-qada): Compensatory performance of a missed ritual after the obstacle is removed.

Dispute on Timing of Hady Slaughter for Muhsar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of hady slaughter for Hajj muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of hady slaughter for a muhsar of Hajj and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
For a muhsar, the hady is a penalty, not a ritual sacrifice—so time is irrelevant except for the Sahibayn.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question: if a pilgrim is prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj, can the required hady be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr, or is it restricted to that specific day? The answer determines when the pilgrim becomes halal and can proceed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is the slaughter of hady by a muhsar of Hajj. The dispute is whether it is permitted only on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or any day before.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa permits slaughter any day before Yawm al-Nahr, analogizing it to other expiatory blood penalties (dam kaffarah) which are restricted to place (Haram) but not time.
Imam Abu Hanifa is the founder of the school.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict slaughter to Yawm al-Nahr for the hady of Hajj, by analogy to the udhiyah sacrifice which is tied to that day. They argue that the hady for Hajj is specific to both place and time.
The Sahibayn agree with Abu Hanifa for Umrah, as no specific day is prescribed.
4
Follow Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa replies that the hady of a muhsar is a penalty (dam kaffarah) for being prevented, not a ritual sacrifice of Hajj. Therefore, it follows the rules of expiatory blood, which are not time-specific.
The key distinction: penalty vs. ritual sacrifice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the muhsar slaughters before Yawm al-Nahr, according to Abu Hanifa he becomes halal immediately and may perform other acts; according to the Sahibayn, the slaughter is invalid and must be repeated on Yawm al-Nahr.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وأما عندهما، فإن كان محصراً بالعمرة فكذا، وإن كان محصراً بالحج لا يجوز الذبح إلا في يوم النحر.
قوله : فكذا ; أي يُعين له يوماً : أي يوم كان، فإن ذبح هدي العمرة لا يختص بيوم النحر اتفاقاً. قوله : إلا في يوم النحر ; لأنّ ذبحه مختص بالزمان المعين كاختصاصه بالمكان المعين. وله : أن هذا الهدي دم كفّارة، فيختص بالمكان دون الزمان، كسائر دماء الكفارات.
This is according to Abu Hanifa. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he is a muhsar of Umrah, then it is similar; but if he is a muhsar of Hajj, slaughter is not permitted except on Yawm al-Nahr. He said: 'So similar': meaning he designates a day, any day. Indeed, slaughter of the hady of Umrah is not specific to Yawm al-Nahr by agreement. He said: 'Except on Yawm al-Nahr': because its slaughter is specific to a designated time just as it is specific to a designated place. And for him (Abu Hanifa): this hady is a blood penalty; thus it is specific to the place but not the time, like other blood penalties for expiations.
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The matn states that the previous ruling (slaughter and compensation) is according to Abu Hanifa. As for the two, if the muhsar is in Umrah, the same ruling applies (they agree). But if he is in Hajj, they hold that slaughter is not valid except on Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah). The commentator explains that for Umrah, any day is fine by agreement. The Sahibayn's proof is that the hady for Hajj is specific to Yawm al-Nahr, just as it is specific to the Haram as a place. Abu Hanifa's response is that this hady is a penalty (dam kaffarah), like other expiation blood, which are specific to place (Haram) but not to a particular time; thus, the sacrifice is valid any time before Yawm al-Nahr as well. The dispute has practical implications: according to Abu Hanifa, the muhsar can slaughter earlier and then perform Hajj, while according to the Sahibayn, he must wait until Yawm al-Nahr, which may affect his ability to perform the pilgrimage.

Key Terms
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice during Hajj.
دم الكفارة (dam al-kaffarah): A blood sacrifice as expiation for a violation or impediment, not a ritual sacrifice of Hajj.
محصر (muhsar): A pilgrim prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to a valid impediment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any day before Yawm al-Nahr
B) Only on Yawm al-Nahr
C) Only after completing Hajj
D) Only at the end of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The hady of a muhsar is a penalty, so its timing is flexible according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.
